The Relationship Between the New Life Movement and Health 122

— Li Tingan

Chairman Chiang promotes the New Life Movement with the aim of revitalizing the nation, with the entire populace as its driving force, and with cleanliness as its primary focus. Indeed, national rejuvenation requires the participation of the entire populace, and the main contribution the entire populace can make to the country is their sound physical health. The cultivation of sound physical health should begin with the initial steps, starting with attention to cleanliness. Therefore, the consistent principle of the New Life Movement promoted by Chairman Chiang is to emphasize fundamentals and be careful at the beginning, and a major component of this chain of emphasizing fundamentals and being careful at the beginning is the cultivation of national health.

There are many ways to achieve health, and the technical methods are even more complex. For example, issues of nutrition, disease prevention, physical examinations, early diagnosis, and physical training are all closely related to the physical and mental health of individuals. Research into these methods are all technical issues. However, if we want to train the entire populace to move towards the realm of national health in an orderly manner, we must not disregard the order of priorities, leading to confusion and counterproductive haste. Therefore, we must distinguish between the important and the less important, and start the training from the most basic points that are most relevant to the daily life of the populace. That is, cleanliness. Since the main component of the New Life Movement is national health, this link of national health in the chain of the New Life Movement is different from ordinary health issues and must be connected by the fundamental principles that run through the entire movement. In other words, any aspect of the New Life Movement must start small and proceed gradually. Training in health should not involve empty talk of lofty ideals, but rather focus on laying solid foundations. It is fitting that the ignorant do not understand its essence and instead ridicule it as superficial. Little do they know that what is ridiculed as superficial is precisely the greatness of the spirit of the New Life Movement.

Cleanliness is indeed of great importance to life. For example, frequent bathing can keep the body's blood flowing smoothly. After our food is digested by the stomach and intestines, the absorbable nutrients are transported to various tissues of the body via the lymphatic vessels and blood. After oxidation, they supply the needs of life, producing various toxic waste products in the process of oxidation. The main ones are carbonic acid, urea, uric acid, etc. Carbon dioxide is expelled from the body by the lungs, while urea and uric acid are excreted with water by the urinary system or through the sweat glands of the skin. Over time, although the water can evaporate, sweat stains (such as urea and various bases) often accumulate at the openings of the glands. If not diligently washed away, they can easily block the openings, losing the function of draining waste and regulating body temperature, thus easily leading to illness. If one is diligent in bathing, this harm can be eliminated. Therefore, the New Life Covenant says: "Bathe often." Also, washing hands before meals and after defecation may seem like a minor matter, but the hands are often in contact with external objects and can easily carry various germs. If hands are not washed before eating, there is a possibility of bringing germs into the mouth. Our feces often contain germs as well. If hands are washed after defecation, the germs can be prevented from re-entering the mouth. Therefore, the New Life Covenant says: "Wash hands often." Furthermore, the cleanliness of teeth is most important. If food accumulates and rots in the gaps between the teeth, it will not only cause yellow teeth and bad breath, but also damage the teeth and lead to dental diseases. If one suffers from dental diseases or tooth roots rot and breed bacteria, the bacteria can enter the stomach and cause stomach diseases, which is greatly harmful. Therefore, the New Life Covenant says: "Rinse mouth after meals, brush teeth every morning." Respiratory diseases such as colds and tuberculosis are spread by droplets expelled from the mouth and nose, such as fine mist, which can infect others when inhaled. If one turns away and covers the mouth and nose with a handkerchief when sneezing or coughing, the expelled droplets will not fly into the air. Therefore, the New Life Covenant says: "Always carry a handkerchief." These few examples show that although these are all very small matters, they are all of great importance to the health of individuals and the public. It also shows that these seemingly minor habits have not yet been universally developed among our Chinese people and still need to be promoted. The following are the forty-four articles related to health out of the 119 articles of the New Life Covenant, to show the close relationship between the New Life Movement and health.

(1) Nine articles on food:

Do not smoke; do not drink excessively; do not eat snacks; drink several glasses of boiled water early in the morning; do not eat unclean food; do not drink unboiled water; rinse mouth after meals, brush teeth every morning; do not engage in strenuous exercise before or after meals; strive for cleanliness in the kitchen and utensils.

(2) Two articles on clothing:

Clothes should be neat, simple, and clean; always carry a handkerchief.

(3) Twenty-three articles on living:

Houses should be clean and tidy, walls should not be scribbled on, furniture should be simple, windows should be opened often, go to bed and wake up early, rinse mouth, wash hair, and wash hands often, breathe fresh air, engage in appropriate exercise every day, wash fingernails often, bathe often, bedding should be sunned and washed often, pay attention to the cleanliness of children, sweep the house often, dredge ditches often, tables and chairs should be clean, toilets should be clean, mosquitoes should be exterminated, flies should be exterminated, rats should be caught and killed, do not spit everywhere, do not urinate and defecate everywhere, throw garbage in the trash can, every household should sweep the streets in front of their doors every day.

(4) One article on movement:

Do not urinate everywhere.

(5) Three articles on entertainment:

Do not patronize prostitutes, do not dance with dance hostesses, do not read obscene books or look at obscene pictures, choose a proper form of entertainment.

Review and Outlook of the New Life Movement 123

— Wen Chaoji

(1) Dr. Sun Yat-sen advocated for the National Revolution, seeking to rescue the Chinese nation from a feudal society characterized by political corruption, dark education, ineffective laws, moral collapse, and economic bankruptcy, and to achieve a society with clear politics, effective education, effective laws, sound morals, economic equality, and a government of the people, by the people, and for the people.

Dr. Sun Yat-sen dedicated his life to this cause, thereby inspiring the prevailing trend and creating a situation in which, with an indomitable spirit that could not be corrupted by wealth, swayed by poverty, or subdued by force, he led the righteous people of the entire Chinese nation, solidified into an irresistible force, and finally overthrew the evil feudal system of the Qing Dynasty.

Leader Chiang Kai-shek, adhering to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's principles for more than thirty years, absolutely obeyed orders and carried out the revolution when Dr. Sun Yat-sen was alive, and after Dr. Sun Yat-sen's death, he continued his aspirations and vigorously practiced his principles, never slacking for a single day.

Leader Chiang Kai-shek, through the arduous struggles of the revolutionary movement, gained countless practical experiences and realized that to implement the entire legacy as soon as possible, it was necessary to first have a broad and universal national movement that everyone could participate in, everyone could do, and everyone could benefit from.

This broad and universal movement is the New Life Movement that the Leader advocated last year amidst the victorious suppression of bandits in Jiangxi.

(2) The New Life Movement has been going on for a year now. Looking back on the work of the New Life Movement over the past year, we feel infinite joy and excitement. Since the Leader advocated the New Life Movement in Jiangxi, upholding the forty virtues of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, he hoped that all citizens would base themselves on these essentials and express their orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, and plainness in their actual lives of clothing, food, housing, and transportation. Speed and thoroughness should be shown in order to change the prevailing atmosphere, rejuvenate the nation, and save it from peril. For a year, the whole country has heard the news and followed suit, setting an example. Starting in Nanchang, the results have been the best in the country. The orderliness of the city, the orderliness of the order, and the cleanliness of the citizens all make people look up to them with respect. As for the leaders of the Party, government, military, police, academic, industrial, agricultural, and commercial circles, they are all able to cooperate sincerely to promote the New Life Movement, and they have also received personal guidance from the Leader. All the people of Nanchang are inspired by the Leader's great spirit, and they all sincerely and willingly follow the Leader's guidance. Therefore, it is no accident that Nanchang has achieved such excellent results. This is one aspect.

Furthermore, major cities such as Hankou, Peiping, Luoyang, and the capital have also been able to implement the New Life Movement in accordance with the Leader's "New Life Movement Outline" and "New Life Guidelines." New Life Guidance Teams were organized to practice the New Life Movement themselves on the one hand, and to actively persuade citizens to practice the New Life Movement on the other hand, and to stipulate various matters for compliance with public order and public health. A serious effort was made to promote and implement the general inspection of orderliness and cleanliness, with considerable results. As for the constitutional police jointly formulating measures to implement the New Life Movement and cooperating to diligently guide implementation, this is especially characteristic.

Finally, let's talk about Shanghai. The New Life Movement in Shanghai has been very active. Mayor Wu and leaders from all walks of life, based on the essence of the Leader's New Life Movement, have made earnest efforts to promote it. Since I took over the Public Security Bureau, I have been fortunate to participate in the work of the New Life Movement, following Mayor Wu and leaders from all walks of life. I have never dared to abandon my responsibility in my Bureau and in the places where my personal responsibilities lie. Therefore, at the beginning of my tenure, I followed the provisions of the New Life Movement, starting with the practical implementation in my Bureau. All aspects of daily office work and the private lives of all staff members are required to conform to propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, and to express orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, plainness, speed, and thoroughness. We are now actively urging and promoting it. Other works, such as holding a city-wide general cleanliness inspection jointly with the Health Bureau and rectifying the city's appearance, have also been actively and continuously promoted. We hope that leaders from all walks of life and all citizens will rigorously supervise us so that the New Life Movement can make substantial progress, which would be a great blessing.

Looking back on the work of the New Life Movement over the past year, the results have been very good. Since the Leader advocated it, leaders and organizations from all walks of life across the country have been inspired and have risen up. A broad atmosphere has been established, and all models are gradually in place. The foundation for national rejuvenation lies here.

(3) Looking forward to the future of the New Life Movement, we feel that there is an infinitely good prospect. From now on, I plan to implement the "New Life Movement Outline" and "New Life Guidelines" stipulated by the Leader, as well as the various matters stipulated by the New Life Movement General Association and the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, in conjunction with all relevant parties. The handling of various matters is described as follows:

First, I plan to urge all staff and police officers of the Bureau to earnestly implement the provisions of the New Life Movement in their public and private lives. For example, clothing, food, housing, and transportation must conform to the provisions of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, and must express orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, plainness, speed, and thoroughness at all times. I also plan to conduct inspections, assessments, and exhortations at any time to ensure that all police officers meet the standards of the New Life Movement and develop the spirit of automatically and consistently practicing the New Life Movement.

Second, I plan to instruct the Public Security Sub-bureaus and Stations to urge their subordinate police officers to lead by example in guiding citizens to practice the New Life Movement, stipulating a period for inspecting whether the residents under the jurisdiction of each Sub-bureau and Station are practicing the New Life Movement. Households that can earnestly implement the New Life Movement will be given honorary awards, and those who do not implement the New Life Movement or do not implement it effectively will be given advice with a kind and enthusiastic attitude to ensure that they can implement the New Life Movement.

Third, I plan to schedule a time to hold a city-wide general cleanliness inspection in conjunction with relevant agencies or personnel to ensure that the city is always kept clean, thereby increasing the health of citizens, improving the appearance of the city, enhancing its appearance, and enhancing the international status of our country.

I am determined to gradually implement the above three points this year.

(4) Finally, I sincerely hope that people from all walks of life will, from now on, follow the various matters indicated by the Leader's New Life Movement, practice them personally, practice propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame as individuals, achieve orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, plainness, speed, and thoroughness in daily life, and then practice propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame as groups, and collectively achieve orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, plainness, speed, and thoroughness. Furthermore, all the people of the country should consistently practice propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, and all the people of the country should consistently achieve orderliness, cleanliness, simplicity, plainness, speed, and thoroughness. Only in this way can our nation be revived, and all the humiliations of our country can be completely washed away. This proves that the New Life Movement is a great work to complete our national rejuvenation movement. I urge my compatriots to rise up together and practice the New Life Movement.

The Shanghai Municipal Security Command and its Special Party Headquarters Hold a New Life Cleanliness Campaign 124

On the 21st, all officers and soldiers of the Command mobilized to sweep the streets.

On the 22nd and 23rd, a thorough inspection of internal cleanliness was carried out.

Since Director Yang Huru and Deputy Director Zeng Zesheng took office at the Shanghai Municipal Security Command, they have spared no effort in rectifying the troops. In October last year, He Yingqin, Minister of Military Affairs, passed through Shanghai on his way from Peiping to Nanjing and inspected the Security Force. He praised the efforts of the Command's authorities in education and training. Recently, he specially requested the National Government to award Director Yang the First Class Medal of the Army, Navy, and Air Force to show his encouragement. Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek advocated the New Life Movement the year before last, the Command has been vigorously implementing it. All aspects of the New Life Movement that the military should implement have been fully implemented. The subordinate national forces submit a weekly report on the implementation and review of the New Life Movement for verification and guidance. Over the past year, the Command has achieved great results in management, education, and training. As the anniversary of the New Life Movement approaches, the Command, in conjunction with the Command's Party Headquarters, has prepared a large-scale

Page 14

To carry out a New Life Cleanliness Campaign, scheduled to be held on the 21st, 22nd, and 23rd of this month for three days. At that time, all officers and soldiers of the Command and its subordinate teams will mobilize. On the 21st, they will sweep the streets and thoroughfares in the vicinity of each garrison. On the 22nd and 23rd, a thorough inspection of internal cleanliness will be carried out. At the same time, the sweeping team, the stretcher team, and the propaganda team will be mobilized to promote public awareness and achieve universal results. The various measures that have been formulated are recorded as follows:

Measures for the Shanghai Municipal Security Command and its Special Party Headquarters to Promote the New Life Movement's Cleanliness Campaign. 1. The Shanghai Municipal Security Command and its Special Party Headquarters have formulated these measures in order to promote the New Life Movement's Cleanliness Campaign (hereinafter referred to as the Cleanliness Campaign) and to attract public attention. 2. Based on the various provisions of these measures, all levels of Party Headquarters affiliated with the Command's Party Headquarters and all teams affiliated with the Command will mobilize in unison. 3. The implementation of this Cleanliness Campaign will adopt the following methods: A. Internally, conduct internal affairs inspections and apply the general internal affairs requirements of the military. B. Externally, organize sweeping, stretcher, and propaganda teams to carry out a major cleaning to arouse public awareness. 4. The organizational measures for the sweeping, stretcher, and propaganda teams will be formulated separately. 5. The scope of activities for the sweeping, stretcher, and propaganda teams in the major cleaning will be the scope of the defense area of each team. 6. The implementation of this Cleanliness Campaign, the internal and external inspections, and the cleaning measures will be completed in two days. The implementation of each day's work and the inspection of the work will be carried out simultaneously. 7. In addition to the existing regulations that should be followed for the internal and external work of this Cleanliness Campaign, personnel will be dispatched by the Command and the Special Party Headquarters to be responsible for the inspection work separately. 8. The key points of the Cleanliness Campaign will be formulated separately. 9. After the Cleanliness Campaign has been completed, the Party Headquarters and teams responsible for it should submit separate reports for review.

Measures for the Shanghai Municipal Security Command and its Special Party Headquarters to Promote the New Life Movement's Cleanliness Campaign and Organize Sweeping, Stretcher, and Propaganda Teams. 1. The organization of each team will be based on the Party's district branch and the Command's company as a joint unit. 2. Each unit may form a full team of twelve to twenty teams, depending on the breadth of the area. 3. The tasks and quantity distribution of each full team formed by each unit are as follows: A. Propaganda teams: three to five teams. B. Sweeping teams: five to eight teams. C. Stretcher teams: four to seven teams. 4. The number of people in each team is two to three people. 5. Each unit will be designated by one person from the district branch and one person from the company to be responsible for guidance and command. 6. Each team should prepare the following application tools: A. Sweeping team: two or three bamboo branch brooms per team. B. Stretcher team: one bamboo basket, one iron shovel, and two or three bamboo branch brooms per team. C. Propaganda team: leaflets (prepared by the Command Party Headquarters). 7. In addition to those prepared by the Command Party Headquarters, the remaining application tools for the entire team will be prepared by each unit separately. 8. The full team formed by each unit will be disbanded upon completion of the Cleanliness Campaign.

Key Points of the Work. A. Principles. 1. The significance and purpose of the Cleanliness Campaign of the New Life Movement promoted by the Command and the Command Party Headquarters (hereinafter referred to as the Cleanliness Campaign) is to guide soldiers and party members, promote the masses, cultivate the virtue of cleanliness, and change social customs, so as to achieve the entire requirements of the New Life Movement step by step, revive the nation, and build a new China. 2. The New Life Movement and the Cleanliness Campaign should be based on all the provisions of the Central Committee on the New Life Movement and the "New Life Movement Outline" and "New Life Guidelines" issued by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, focusing on the practical and effective parts related to cleanliness. 3. All personnel participating in the mobilization should know that as party members or soldiers, their words and deeds are all models for the masses. They should uphold the spirit of "setting an example" and achieve the effect of rectifying themselves and rectifying others. B. Individual Requirements. 1. The significance and purpose of the Cleanliness Campaign has been recognized in principle, then the personnel participating in this mobilization must make every effort to promote it and achieve the goal of success. 2. Based on the two items listed in the measures for the Cleanliness Campaign promoted by the Command and the Command Party Headquarters, the following requirements are made separately: A. Internal: The internal work requirements will be specified separately by the Command. B. External: (1) The sweeping and stretcher teams should be responsible for sweeping the streets in the designated areas of activity. When sweeping, they should strive for thoroughness, and pay special attention to the accumulated dirt in the streets and alleys. (2) Those who accumulate sewage and foul odors should do their best to dredge the ditches to facilitate their flow. Those that the sweeping team cannot do should be recorded in detail by the guidance and command personnel for transfer to the competent authorities for handling. (3) The garbage swept up by the stretcher team should be poured into the nearby garbage cans, and special attention should be paid to the cleanliness of the left and right sides of the garbage cans. (4) In addition to distributing leaflets, the propaganda team should explain in detail the significance of the cleaning campaign carried out by the Command in each section that the sweeping team has completed, so as to inspire the public's enthusiasm for cleanliness and to be happy to implement it. (5) When performing their tasks, the propaganda team should give good advice to the public when they encounter behaviors that violate the requirements of cleanliness, so that they are happy to accept them and know how to repent. (6) All personnel performing propaganda tasks should be serious and peaceful in their attitude, whether performing propaganda or exhortation, so as to achieve the function of edification, and should not be aggressive and coercive, so as not to cause resentment. (7) The propaganda team should pay attention to the maintenance of public order when performing propaganda tasks. (8) The guidance and command of each unit should pay attention to the spirit of all team members, and there should be no slackness or listlessness. 3. All personnel participating in the Cleanliness Campaign should abide by the creeds listed by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek: (1) Self-awareness; (2) Determination; (3) Starting with persuasion; (4) Starting with oneself; (5) Saying less and doing more; (6) Doing it at all times; (7) Doing it honestly; (8) Supervising each other; and treat them as a guide and abide by them unswervingly. C. Inspection. 1. All personnel responsible for inspection work should arrive at the designated area on time to carry out the inspection. 2. Check the results of the internal and external work carried out in the area, and evaluate the merits and demerits, and report them separately for rewards and punishments. 3. The inspection personnel should not only seek the actual effect of the work, but also examine the difficulties in the implementation of these measures from time to time, so as to improve them. 4. The internal affairs inspection section will be specified separately by the Command. D. Discipline. 1. All team members of each unit should absolutely obey the orders of the guidance and command. Those who deliberately violate them will be reported truthfully for severe punishment. 2. If the spirit of the team members of each unit is depressed and hinders the reputation of the team, the guidance should immediately warn them. If they do not listen to the warning, they should be ordered to return to the team first, and then reported for punishment. E. Precautions. 1. All personnel participating in the Cleanliness Campaign should pay attention to the following points: a. Serious attitude; b. Neat military uniform; c. Loyalty to their duties; d. Do not spit everywhere; e. Do not urinate everywhere; f. Do not joke or scold; g. Do not eat snacks; h. Face and hands should be clean; i. The propaganda should be concise. F. 1. The relationship between cleanliness and life is very important, because it is not only for the sake of appearance, but also for the sake of health. The spirit of mankind is also manifested from it. 2. The meaning of promoting cleanliness is to improve appearance, promote health, and revitalize the spirit, so that a healthy individual can develop a healthy nation and country, so as to adapt to survival in this world. 3. The key to the success of the Cleanliness Campaign lies in the concerted mobilization and efforts of all citizens, and it is only with continuous efforts that there is hope. Our work this time is just to open the door for all citizens. We only hope that we can extend from the work of a few people to the work of many people, from our small-scale work to large-scale work. This is our sincere hope. G. Slogans: (1) All citizens unite to promote the New Life Movement! (2) Neatness and simplicity are the conditions for implementing the New Life Movement! (3) The New Life should start with clothing, food, housing and transportation to achieve neatness and simplicity! (4) Work with renewed efforts to remove the old and bring in the new! (5) Expand the Cleanliness Campaign! (6) Only a healthy people can have a healthy nation and a healthy country! (7) Revitalize the Chinese nation!

The Envoy to Turkey, He Yaozu, Will Go Abroad to Assume Office on Schedule 127

Sent Counselor Wang Pengsheng to Turkey to Prepare in Advance

The Sino-Turkish Commercial Treaty Will Await His Arrival to Solicit Opinions

The newly appointed Envoy to Turkey, He Yaozu, arrived in Shanghai on the special night express train at one quarter past five yesterday morning. He is staying at the Yipinxiang Hotel on Tibet Road. He came to visit Minister of Finance Kong due to his illness and to discuss the embassy's expenses. He returned to Beijing that evening and is scheduled to go abroad to take office on the thirteenth of next month. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency paid a special visit yesterday. According to the interview, the details are as follows:

Going to Take Office on Schedule

Since receiving the government's appointment, I have been actively preparing everything. Originally, I planned to go to take office today, but due to the embassy's expenses not being finalized, it has been delayed again and again. Now, it is tentatively scheduled to travel on the Italian postal ship "Conte Rosso" on the thirteenth of next month. Initially, it was planned to send Secretary Ma Hongdao to Turkey in advance to prepare for the embassy site, etc. Now, Mr. Ma has been replaced by Counselor Wang Pengsheng, who is currently in London, England, to rush to Turkey.

Expense Budget

Regarding the embassy's expenses, the budget has been roughly finalized and has been approved by the Executive Yuan and is currently awaiting approval from the Central Political Council. The amount is roughly the same as that of the embassy in Japan. However, the exact amount has not yet been officially notified by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so it is not convenient to announce. My purpose here is to visit Minister of Finance Kong due to his illness. The embassy's expenses may be discussed at the same time.

Embassy Organization

As for the embassy's organization, there are Counselor Wang Pengsheng, Secretaries He Fengshan, Li Ju, Wang Shifu, Ma Hongdao, Attaché Lu Feng, and Chiefs Li Yaoyu and Yao Zhuxiu. These officials have all been appointed. Except for Counselor Wang, who will go to Turkey from London first, the rest will travel with me. In addition, my young son will also accompany me, but my wife will not go. As for the military attachés, they are appointed by the General Staff Headquarters. Whether the candidates have been finalized is unknown because it does not fall under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The location of the embassy will be in Ankara.

Sino-Turkish Commercial Treaty

In order to promote business between the two countries, it is necessary to sign a Sino-Turkish commercial treaty. However, I do not yet know whether I will be instructed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to proceed with this upon my arrival. Generally, a decision will be made after I arrive in Turkey and exchange opinions with the authorities of that country. I have only just been appointed, so I have little to announce at the moment. After I arrive, I will strive to promote the relationship between China and Turkey so as not to fail the government's trust.

Several Telegram Lines in Shanghai, Hankou, and Guangzhou Have Been Repaired 129

Interrupted for More Than Ten Years

Announcements Started Yesterday

According to the East China News Agency, the telegraph line from Hankou to Guangzhou of the Ministry of Communications has not been repaired since it was interrupted ten years ago. All telegrams from Hankou to Guangdong were forwarded through Jiangxi. Telegrams from Shanghai to Guangdong, except for wireless telegrams, were sent through the three companies' submarine cables. After several transfers, the time was inevitably delayed. Now, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the staff of the telegraph bureaus in each section to work overtime to rush repairs, which has been going on for some time. Yesterday, a spokesperson from the telegraph bureau told the East China News Agency reporter that the direct line between Guangdong and Hankou has been repaired and direct notifications have been restored since yesterday. All wired telegrams from Shanghai to Guangdong will also be forwarded through Hankou and should arrive within one hour, it is said.

A Tourist Group to the Philippines Will Board the Ship Tonight to Set Sail 130

A Total of Twenty-Seven People Led by Wang Xiaolai

The Chamber of Commerce Sends a Special Telegram to the Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce

The Hong Kong Chamber of Commerce Will Prepare to Receive Them When They Pass Through Hong Kong

The Chinese tourist group to the Philippines is scheduled to board the ship tonight and set sail tomorrow morning. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce and Consul General Deng to report that the group will make a short stopover in Hong Kong. The details are as follows:

Boarding the Ship Tonight and Setting Sail Tomorrow Morning

The Chinese tourist group to the Philippines has a total of twenty-seven people. The head of the group, Wang Rutang, has already gone to the Philippines from Shanghai a few days ago. The remaining twenty-six members, led by the deputy head of the group, Wang Xiaolai, are scheduled to board the Dollar Steamship Company's President Jackson tonight and set sail from Shanghai to the Philippines tomorrow morning. All members have prepared everything. Representatives from various industries in Shanghai will go to the pier to see them off. When passing through Hong Kong, they plan to disembark for a short stay before boarding the original ship to the Philippines. They are scheduled to return to Shanghai on the Dollar Steamship Company's President Wilson on March 4th. It is also reported that they want to board the ship today. The last two ferries are at 9:00 PM and 12:30 AM. All members can entrust the China Travel Service to take care of their luggage and board the ship in advance, which is more convenient.

A Short Stopover in Hong Kong

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Hong Kong Chinese Chamber of Commerce the day before yesterday, saying that the Chinese tourist group to the Philippines decided to depart on the President Jackson on the 24th and is scheduled to return to Shanghai on the President Wilson on March 4th. The group members include Wang Zhengting, Wang Xiaolai, and his wife, totaling twenty-seven people. They plan to make a short stopover in Hong Kong. Please provide hospitality. Civil Servants Will Also Be Inspected

Those Who Disobey Can Be Punished

Recently, piracy has been rampant, and cases of hijacking merchant ships have occurred frequently. In the past few days, pirates have been mixed on various ships, plotting to rob. The captains of the Chuanshan, Zhoushan, Yili, Daxing, Taizhou, and other ships in this port have jointly petitioned for the inspection of public officials to prevent pirates from disguising themselves and mixing in. The original petition was submitted to the Zhejiang military police authorities by Fan Shangda, captain of Zhoushan, Zhou Shengli, captain of Yili, Zhuo Shiding, captain of Daxing, Zhang Jiuzhi, captain of Taizhou, Zhang Hecheng, captain of Chuanshan, and Lu Yizhi, captain of Dahua. Pirate Ship Hijackings Are Becoming More and More Serious

Inspection is not easy and it is easy to see the traces, which leads to this. Although the water and land police strictly check each ship upon arrival, it is easier to start searching ordinary people. However, for passengers wearing military uniforms, there are not a few who restrain themselves and submit to inspection, but there are really many who are unreasonable and resist stubbornly. Rely on Their Dignity as Inviolable

Thinking of this, they couldn't help but shudder. After discussion by Shangda and others, the only way is to petition the water and land military police authorities and other administrative and judicial agencies. When military police or public officials take a boat, please

Issue a Pass and Arrange Numbers

When disembarking, they must wear it uniformly, and please describe the style of the pass and post it on each ship. If you encounter a naval police inspection, you should hand over the pass and not make any unreasonable resistance, so that the service personnel of each ship can recognize it and facilitate inspection, then bandits will also find it difficult to trace. The benefits to the shipping merchants are not small, and so on. After the military police agencies signed and submitted their opinions, it was believed that in the case of ship hijackings in recent years, the bandits were disguised as passengers. The Naval Police Check and Identify Easily

The intention is very good, but it is related to the administration of the whole province. Military, police, and military agencies and public officials have official business or leave to return home. Except for special tasks and confidential documents, there are badges and documents to prove it. There is no need to issue a pass. Public officials, whether or not there are the above-mentioned badges and documents, shall be allowed to conduct legal inspections if they are confirmed to be suspected of carrying contraband. If they deliberately resist, they shall be reported to the competent authority for strict punishment (omitted below).

The above points are our hope for Mr. Mei's trip, which is not only Mr. Mei's responsibility, but also the original intention of the Soviet Union's invitation. They were deeply gratified.

Mei Lanfang's Reply

Dr. Mei Lanfang replied, "Chairman, gentlemen, I am very honored and grateful to have you gentlemen here today to see me off. I will never forget the words of encouragement and praise that you have just said, and I dare not be worthy of the praise. I remember four years ago, when I went to the United States, I also received guidance and support from you gentlemen. Now that I am going to the Soviet Union, I am still receiving the enthusiasm of you gentlemen, so that our country's drama can be promoted outside the country, so that Lanfang can also achieve many years of ambition. This is what Lanfang is very grateful for. This trip to Russia has been brewing for almost a year. As early as February last year, the Soviet government asked our country's embassy in Russia to invite Lanfang to perform. At that time, Lanfang did not dare to agree, because the Soviet Union is a country with the greatest literature, drama, and music. Since the revolution, their government has been vigorously promoting it, so the achievements have been rapid. If Lanfang goes to Russia, of course, he can take this opportunity to visit and study, and maybe he can get a little knowledge, but on the other hand, I am really afraid that my ability is not enough, and I am afraid that I cannot contribute the essence of Chinese drama to others, so I did not dare to agree immediately. Later, the Soviet Union repeatedly invited me, and telegrams and letters were sent in succession. They said that they wanted Lanfang to perform completely for research purposes. The meaning in the letter was very sincere. The government of our country, when Ambassador Yan heard about it, also advocated that Lanfang should agree because of diplomatic relations, so Lanfang dared to reluctantly take on the task. After the decision, the government authorities and Ambassador Yan and other gentlemen gave all kinds of assistance. The gentlemen in Shanghai also organized a drama association to guide and support, which was very enthusiastic. Lanfang is very grateful. Mr. Shi Liangcai, who first initiated the drama association, did not wait for Lanfang to go abroad, and he parted with us forever. Today, I cannot hear Mr. Shi's admonitions, which is something that Lanfang feels very sad about. Lanfang is very worried about this trip to Russia. Why? Because the performance methods of drama in the East and the West are completely different, and as I said just now, the Soviet Union is also a country with the greatest literature and drama. Can Lanfang's performance satisfy the people of the Soviet Union? So I feel very suspicious. I still hope that the gentlemen present today will give more guidance. This is what Lanfang is most looking forward to. After Lanfang performs in Russia, he will also go to various European countries to visit their dramas. However, whether he can have any insights after returning to China and report them is really uncertain. Speaking of it, I really feel very ashamed. Lanfang and the troupe have decided to accompany Ambassador Yan on a ship sent by the Soviet Union the day after tomorrow, all the way to Vladivostok, and then take the Siberian train to Moscow from Vladivostok. The time is very short. Just these two days, they have performed a few days of charity performances, so they don't have time to go to each of you gentlemen to say goodbye. Today, I will take this opportunity to say goodbye to you gentlemen, and when I return to China in the future, I will report everything to you gentlemen. Today, I thank you for your kindness and wish you all good health."

City Government Chemical Examination of Fire Well Truth 135

Underground Coal Quietly Awaits Reaction to Produce Marsh Gas

Thus, the Amount of Heat Accumulated Must Be Measured and Surveyed

The fire well at the Taizhou Guild Hall in this city, since it was discovered and announced by a reporter from the East China News Agency, has attracted a large number of onlookers. People in the community have also made various speculations, believing that there is a large amount of fire underground, which will be like a volcanic eruption. People in Shanghai have petitioned the city government to conduct a chemical examination. If there is accumulated heat, it can be extracted as fuel; otherwise, it would be a pity to abandon it. The city government has now sent personnel to conduct a chemical examination, and the result is that the underground of the fire well emits marsh gas due to the reaction of garbage, coal dust, etc. The heat is very weak and cannot be used as fuel. The results of the city government's chemical examination are recorded below.

Dispatching Personnel for Chemical Examination

After the discovery of the fire well last month, citizens such as Zhang Yin of this city immediately petitioned the city government to conduct a chemical examination. If it is natural heat accumulated underground, it can be used as industrial fuel. The city government, according to the petition, immediately sent personnel from the Industrial Testing Institute of the Social Affairs Bureau to conduct a chemical examination a few days ago, and the results are already available.

Cause of Fire

According to the analysis results of the bureau, the gas is marsh gas, commonly known as "natural gas," which is an organic substance generated by decay. It is thought that the guild hall is adjacent to Lujia浜 (creek). In recent years, the 浜 (creek) has been filled with garbage and coal dust. The garbage undergoes decomposition under the action of moisture, mixed pressure, and heat, forming this kind of gas. The chemical examination results are listed below. It escapes through cracks and penetrates the ground. The original abandoned well of the guild hall may be in the right place, and the ejection pressure is not strong, and the heat is very weak, making it difficult to use for industrial purposes. As for whether the underground storage is abundant, it must be determined by expert surveys.

Chemical Examination Results

The Industrial Testing Institute announced the various components contained in the fire well as follows: Marsh gas (Methane) 6.7%, Hydrogen (Hydrogen Hz) 12.8%, Nitrogen (Nitrogen Hz) 13.86%, Carbon Dioxide (Carbon Dioxide Coz) 2.18%, Carbon Monoxide (Carbon Monoxide Co.) 0.10%, Heating Value (Heating Valen s410.iikg Cal/liter)

Heavy Fog Permeated Yesterday Morning 136

Streetcars Move Slowly, Shops Burn Lights

Large Numbers of Jianghai Steamers Blocked Outside the Mouth

This port experienced heavy fog again yesterday morning. It was difficult to distinguish people at a slightly longer distance. The fog was especially heavy outside the Wusongkou (Wusong Port), causing rice and Shanghai steamers to be blocked outside the mouth. The situation is recorded below.

Seen in Heavy Fog

Last winter, this port experienced several heavy fogs. Since the beginning of spring, although there have been very few sunny days, heavy fog has not yet been seen. After dawn yesterday morning, heavy fog suddenly descended. By 8 o'clock, the fog became even thicker, making it difficult to distinguish people a few steps away. Streetcars moved slowly, and shops had to burn lights to operate. In addition, because the sunlight was blocked by the fog, the red color was like blood. Staring at it for a long time, the light was faintly visible.

Steamers Blocked Outside the Mouth

The heavy fog began to dissipate after 10 o'clock, causing water traffic to be hindered during this time. According to investigations from the Jianghai Customs and various shipping companies, as of 10 o'clock, the Customs steamer import license did not have a single word on it, indicating that a large number of steamers were blocked by the fog outside the mouth. According to investigations, the steamers blocked included the President Jefferson of the Dollar Steamship Company (from Japan to Shanghai), the General Pershing of the Pacific Mail Steamship Company (from Japan to Shanghai), the Tsukuba Maru of the Pacific Mail Steamship Company (from Hong Kong to Shanghai), and the Bomei Maru (from Japan to Shanghai). As for the Yangtze River steamers, there was the China Merchants Jiangda Steamer. The above-mentioned steamers only entered the port successively after the fog cleared, and their berthing time was all in the afternoon.

Zhou Zhonghong's Descendants Litigate Over Ancestral Hall Property After His Martyrdom for Dredging the Wusong River 139

How to Treat Ancestors and the Locality

Judge Advises Mutual Concessions

Zhou Zhonghong, who served as the Zhifu (Prefect) of Songjiang Prefecture during the reign of Emperor Yongzheng of the Qing Dynasty, whose style name was Zizhen, later died in office due to supervising the dredging of the Wusong River. At that time, the gentry and people of Songjiang and Shanghai, recalling his virtues, built ancestral halls to repay his merits. By the eighth year of Daoguang, the Governor-General of Liangjiang, Jiang Youxian, and the Governor of Jiangsu, Tao Zhu, had posthumously awarded Zhou the title of Taipu Si (Grand Master of the Palace). During the Xianfeng period, the Shanghai Zhixian (Magistrate) Liu Qiu膏 again purchased 70 mu of ancestral hall property as fields, so that his descendants could collect rent to be used as expenses for the Spring and Autumn sacrificial rites. Currently, this field property is managed by Zhou Dadong of the Nomura Lumber Company at No. 86, Guangdong Road. Now, Zhou Shuzhi, Zhou Xueyu, Zhou Xuedan, Zhou Xuechu, Zhou Yuxian, Zhou Yuxiu, Zhou Rongcai, Zhou Qiuchi, Zhou Huanwen, etc., have jointly retained lawyer Zhang Ji to file a lawsuit against Zhou Dadong in the First Special District District Court for infringement of sacrificial property, claiming that the rental income from the sacrificial property, in addition to the sacrificial expenses, belongs to the descendants of the ancestral hall. It has always been handled according to the original plan. Initially, Zhou Dadong's uncle, Xinyuan, managed it. After Xinyuan's death, the defendant began to manage it. The plaintiffs and the defendant are both descendants of the Taipu Gong, so the ancestral hall property should be jointly owned by the plaintiffs and the defendant. However, since the defendant took over the management, the land price has been rising, and with great profits, he has gradually harbored the malicious intention of turning it into his personal property, changing the sacrificial field to his personal household name and independently disposing of it and privately renting it to foreign merchants. If they do not come out and claim the right to joint ownership, they will be deprived of it. For this reason, they request that the defendant Zhou Dadong hand over all the property certificates of the ritual fields and allow the plaintiffs and others to jointly manage it. The so-called renting to foreign merchants refers to Nomura Lumber Company. The company was founded by the Japanese, and Zhou Dadong is currently employed there. Zhou has a relationship with the company as host and guest, and there is no lack of considerable affection between them. Before filing the lawsuit, Zhou Hengzhi and others repeatedly investigated the details of the lease from the company, but to no avail. Therefore, they specifically requested in the complaint that the court notify the Japanese consul to investigate the contents of the lease with the company. Zhou Dadong also retained lawyers Yuan Yang'an and others to make a statement in defense after being accused, claiming that his great-grandfather, Peiwen, had served as the Fengsi Sheng (Sacrificial Student) in the Songjiang Zhou Ancestral Hall and had also been ordered by the Songjiang Prefecture and Shanghai County to be the Fengsi Sheng of the Shanghai Zhou Ancestral Hall. From his grandfather to his father to himself, he has guarded his position for generations. All the ancestral hall property was ordered by the Prefecture and County to be managed by the descendants of the ancestral hall. His father, Xinyuan, also paid the field price to the Shangbao Shatian Official Property Bureau and filed it with the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau, obtaining ownership. It is definitely not something that other clansmen can covet. Moreover, this property was originally donated by local gentry and people and is specifically used for the annual repairs of the Shanghai Zhou Ancestral Hall and the salary of the Fengsi Sheng. It is not the inheritance of Zhonghong Gong, nor is it jointly owned by the descendants of Zhonghong Gong. The plaintiffs are not descendants of the Zhou Ancestral Hall. From where did they obtain the right of joint ownership? Moreover, Zhou Shuchun and Zhou Bingjun previously impersonated descendants of the ancestral hall to covet the ancestral hall property and had already reported it to the city government for protection, making it clear that other clansmen could not recklessly contend for it. It is obvious. He humbly asks to reject the original lawsuit. Yesterday morning, the judge of the First Special Court, Mo Runhua, opened a court to summon and interrogate. The lawyers of both parties made their statements in turn. Judge Mo believed that both parties belonged to the same clan and should be mindful of mutual concessions. He then persuaded both parties to go outside and try to reconcile. If there was no room for reconciliation, a date would be set for further investigation.

Da Hu Bank Runner Cheats for Overdraft Funds 141

Privately Establishes Securities Firm to Overdraft from Da Hu

Fails in Operating Gold Speculation and Cotton Yarn Business

Qian Guanxian, a native of Ningbo, has been working as a runner at the Da Hu Bank at No. 510 Nanjing Road, with a monthly salary of 70 yuan, specializing in credit and loan matters. In January of last year, Deyu Securities Firm in Room 205, Securities Building, Hankou Road, applied to the bank for credit and overdraft of 5,000 yuan. The bank then ordered Qian to investigate. After Qian's investigation, he replied to the manager, saying that the firm was established by Chai Chuan貴, the president of Jiande Bank, and had excellent credit. The bank immediately approved Deyu's request and opened an account. By the end of last year's lunar calendar, Deyu Firm owed the Da Hu Bank an overdraft of 4,461.19 yuan. At that time, Qian suddenly disappeared from the bank. The deputy manager of Da Hu, Wang Hong赍, sent someone to the firm to collect the debt, but the firm had already closed down. There was only a Yan surnamed apprentice inside. When asked who the owner of Deyu Firm was, he replied that it was Qian Guanxian. Da Hu then realized that it had been deceived and reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station for investigation. Detective Wang Shanqing of the Chinese Detective Division went to Qian's residence on Tiantong Road to arrest him, but to no avail. Recently, it was discovered that Qian was often at No. 26, Lane 601, Zhoujiazui Road. Therefore, the detective waited there and arrested him on the previous day and took him back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the situation and prosecuted him for breach of trust under Article 366 of the Criminal Law. Da Hu also retained lawyer Hua Maosheng to appear in court. When interrogated, Qian Guanxian confessed that the Deyu firm was jointly established by him and Chai Chuan贵 with a capital of 10,000 yuan, operating securities, gold speculation, and cotton yarn businesses. Due to losses amounting to tens of thousands of yuan, it was unable to maintain operations. He did not deny the overdraft of more than 4,400 yuan from the Da Hu Bank. He also retained lawyers Fan Gang and Fan Qisheng to defend him. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the confession and, believing that the case still needed investigation, ordered a postponement of the hearing for a week. The defendant was returned to custody.

Investigation Outline: After attending the Soviet International Film Exhibition, Zhou also plans to conduct a detailed investigation of the Soviet film industry and has already drawn up the following investigation outline: (1) The current Soviet film administrative jurisdiction organs, organization system, film censorship, tax rules, import procedures, etc.; (2) Current status of the film industry; (3) Film schools; (4) Construction and equipment of photography studios; (5) Movie theaters; (6) Music and drama; (7) Related film books and magazines; (8) Whether there is a market for Chinese films; (9) Soviet impressions and criticisms of China's participation in the exhibition; (10) Opinions of overseas Chinese on domestic films; (11) The course of the Soviet International Film Exhibition; (12) Others.

Reason for Wang Boying's Kidnapping 145

Instigated by Wang's Friend Yin Zhibai's Chauffeur Ma Shenzhong

After Being Kidnapped, Ma Secretly Inquired About All Movements of the Wang Family

Wang Boying, manager of Da Ji Money Exchange and director of Da Dong Bookstore, was suddenly kidnapped by bandits at the entrance of Changfeng Lane, Tongyun Road, on the evening of the 9th of this month and hidden at No. 14, Rongfu Lane, West Aihans Road, French Concession, and sent a letter demanding a ransom of 200,000 yuan. After the case, the Chinese and Western detectives of the Chengdu Road Police Station arrested the bandits Wang Liugen, Wang Cai氏, Zhang Zhengguo, and Yang Kong氏, and killed one bandit named Yao Maoqing on the spot, rescued the hostage, and sent them to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now known that the Chinese detectives Feng Baishun, Cui Chengke, and Huang Fusen, Xu Dezhong, and others who handled the case have been working hard to investigate for several days and have made further progress, and have arrested the insider Ma Shenzhong, a native of Nanjing, and his accomplice Hu Amao (ie, coppersmith Amao), a native of Jiading, the day before yesterday. Ma has been working as a chauffeur for Yin Zhibai at No. 9, Gui仁 Lane, Maigen Road. Yin and Wang Boying are friends and neighbors and often visit each other. Therefore, Ma is very familiar with Wang Boying's family situation, as well as the residence of his beloved concubine and when he enters and exits. He colluded with Wang Liugen and others to carry out the kidnapping. Afterwards, he also instigated the bandits to send a letter to his master Yin Zhibai, asking him to help the hostage prepare the money, and secretly inquired about the Wang family's movements, whether they had reported it to the police or were willing to pay the ransom. Because Ma and the hostage knew each other, it was inconvenient for him to show his face in the bandit's den. Therefore, Ma hired Hu Amao to act as a go-between. If they got the ransom in the future, they would share it according to the shares. The method was very clever. However, the heavens are just, and the detectives found out the secret, so Ma was arrested and detained. The police sent Ma and Gu to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court yesterday morning, requesting permission to detain them and try them together with Wang Liugen and others. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin explained the above situation, saying that Ma Shenzhong was confessed by the arrested criminal Wang Liugen, and Hu Amao was confessed by Ma, so he was arrested, and requested to be tried together. When interrogated, Ma confessed that he had been a chauffeur at Yin Zhibai's house for three or four years. Yin and Wang Boying were friends and often interacted, so he was familiar with Wang's family situation. This kidnapping case was first discussed in Wen 室 on the second floor of the Dacheng Apartment. Wang Liugen and the deceased were both present, and they asked me about the time and place of the hostage's entry and exit, which I told them. I was not present during the kidnapping, and I had never been to the bandit's den in Rongfu Lane. Only the day after Wang was kidnapped, I saw the news in the newspaper and learned that they had already started. So, I sent Hu Amao to the bandit's den to find out the situation. I learned that the hostage was guarded by Wang 貿根 and the deceased. A day later, Wang Liugen asked Amao to come and told me to go. Because it was inconvenient for me, I met at Room 56 of the Siming Hotel. Wang told me that the hostage was very anxious to get out, and although he had contacted him by phone, there was no result, and asked me about the recent situation of the Wang family, whether they had reported it to the police, and I replied that I didn't know. When questioned, Hu Amao confessed that he was entrusted by Ma, which was not denied. After Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the confession, he ordered Ma and Hu to be detained and tried together with Wang Liugen and others on Friday afternoon.

North and South Rice Trade Associations in Shanghai Halt Transactions Yesterday to Discuss the Issue of Final Payments in Silver Dollars 146

Attended by Over a Hundred Member Representatives

Petitioning the Social Affairs Bureau for Relief

The North and South Rice Trade Associations of the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Guild halted transactions yesterday to address the issue of collecting final payments from rice shops in silver dollars. Over one hundred and seventy member representatives attended the general meeting, resolving to adopt a signing system for future final payment transactions in silver dollars, and to submit a petition to the Social Affairs Bureau for record-keeping and relief. Details are as follows:

Halt of Transactions for One Day

The North and South Rice Trade Associations of the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Guild, in preparation for the joint meeting of the association on the 15th of this month regarding the collection of final payments in silver dollars, halted transactions for one day yesterday. The general meeting of all members of the North and South Rice Trade Associations was convened at the Cuixiu Hall in the Yuyuan Garden in the city at 1:00 PM, resulting in no rice market yesterday.

Convening of the General Meeting

Following the confirmation by the joint meeting, an emergency general meeting of members was convened yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. Representatives from member firms, including Yu Yuan, Yi Yuan, Yong Da, Wan Xing, Xin Chang, Yi Xing Feng, Yi Chang Xing, Xin Xing Chun, Yuan Yu, He Feng Tai, Rui Chang Fa, De Feng, San Tai, Yi Shun Xing, Cheng Feng, Cheng Tai, Da Da, Yu Da De, Tong Xing Yong, Yu Sheng Gong, Da Fa, Yi Xing, Yong Shun Tai, Yu Chang Tai, Ju Xing Cheng, Yu Da De, Da Chang Shen, Wan Tai Xiang, Yuan Shun, Wan Sheng Tai, Xie Chang De, Wan Sheng Xing, Yu Tai Xing, Yuan Yu, Yuan Sheng Chang, Ding Tai Mei, Yi Tai Xiang, Hua Da, Tong Xing Yong, Ding Tai De, Yuan Mao, Wan Xing, Yuan Sheng Run, Ju Tai, San Tai, Run Shou Feng, Heng Xing Xie, Xie Kang, Jian Ting, Ding Feng, Yong Feng, Heng Xing Yi, Wei Yuan Feng, Hong Sheng, Rui Kang, Heng Chang Yi, Tong Tai, Heng Yi Gong, Xin Chang, and others, totaling over one hundred and seventy people, including Gu Xin Yi, Zhu Zi Xiang, and Yan Xiao Quan, attended.

Important Matters Resolved

Chaired by Gu Xin Yi, the discussion focused on changing the final payment from small silver to large silver. (Traditionally, transactions between rice shops and rice merchants involved rounding off amounts less than one yuan, with ten small silver coins considered one yuan. Rice shops often used double silver coins to represent silver dollars when paying rice merchants for three to four dan of rice.) During the meeting, representatives from various member firms expressed their opinions. After three o'clock, a consensus had not yet been reached. Finally, the majority agreed, and for the sake of prudence, decided to use a signing system, where those who signed would implement final payments in silver dollars, and those who did not would indicate their opposition. The result was that eight out of ten agreed to switch to silver dollars.

Petition for Relief

Furthermore, the association, deeply concerned that the issue of final payments might lead to unrest, decided to submit the important matters discussed yesterday to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval and record-keeping, before implementing them on a set date. According to a committee member of the association, speaking to a reporter from Hua Dong News Agency, although the final payment issue has existed since the market began, it has always been in small silver. However, at a time when all commodities are generally priced in silver dollars, if the rice industry continues with the old practices, the losses to rice merchants would be significant. Moreover, rice shops sell to consumers in silver dollars, regardless of whether it is calculated by the dan, dou, sheng, or he. It is reasonable to forgive the rice merchants for changing the final payment from small silver to large silver.

Ge has written a report stating that friends and colleagues had lent him money, and that his assets could repay about half of the amount. District Court Destroys Narcotics 150

The Shanghai District Court Prosecutor's Office confiscated illegal narcotics from various police stations, such as opium and caffeine, from July 1 to the end of December. The total amount included 431 catties and 199 taels and 1 fen of opium, 8,678 taels of fake opium, 18 catties and 10 taels of opium dross, 3,867 red pills and 67 catties and 36 taels of red pills, 3 catties and 15 taels of morphine, 1,034 opium bubbles, 2 catties and 10 taels of opium paste, and 2,748 pieces of opium paraphernalia and ashes. The number of items was not counted for sealed items with specified weights; multiple items combined in a sealed package were counted as one item, whether it was a package of opium pills or a small amount of opium bubble. Chief Prosecutor Zhong Shangbin had already created a register and reported it. Based on the instruction No. 4033 from the Chief Prosecutor of the Jiangsu High Court, it was decided to publicly burn the narcotics on the 18th of this month. Chief Prosecutor Zhong sent letters to various agencies, requesting them to send personnel to supervise the event. Yesterday was the designated date. At 1:00 PM, representatives arrived successively, including Yu Hao from the Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor's Office, Ju Zhijing and Zhou Daguang from the First Special District Court, Wang Sima and Zhao Yifen from the Second Special District Court, Huang Yunshu from the Shanghai Municipal Government, Zhao Wanli from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Lu Zonghan from the Jianghai Customs, Ren Bin from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Chen Shisheng from the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, and Xu Yuyin from the Shanghai County Public Patrol Bureau. Chief Prosecutor Zhong, accompanied by Dean Shen, welcomed the representatives and led them to the living room for a brief conversation. Chief Prosecutor Zhong then instructed judicial police chief Chen Junfang and police officers Chen Xihui and Gu Hanqing to supervise all bailiffs in transporting the confiscated narcotics from the exhibit storage to the open space behind the court, where they were piled up. Meanwhile, Chief Prosecutor Zhong led the representatives to the thatched shed erected behind the court to begin counting and verifying the items. Chen ordered the police to place all the narcotics on pine firewood, sprinkle them with kerosene and salt, and set them on fire. The flames soared into the air. After three bell rings, the burning was completed. The representatives took their leave. The remaining ashes were placed in hemp bags and transported to the Huangpu River to be discarded, in order to eliminate the toxic fumes.

Regarding the news item published in the local news column of today's (18th) newspaper, which stated, "Several police officers from this team found a boat loaded with a large quantity of red pills (estimated to be worth several thousand yuan) on the Pujiang bank of the Dada Pier, and detained a man transporting the drugs," after reading it, it is not true. Special Article

Opinions and Hopes Regarding the New Life Movement 158

— Zhang Yuanruo

Any movement, the movement itself, is not our goal, but merely a method to promote a certain goal. Meetings, speeches, and newspaper publicity are only means of the movement, not the purpose of the movement. Any advocate of a movement, if he mistakes the means for the end, will inevitably fail. (See my book, "The Qualities That Advocates of the New Life Movement Should Possess," Chen Bao, 23, 11, 21.)

China's recent history has an important feature that is "movement-oriented." The purpose of past movements was undoubtedly to save the country from its perilous state and revive the dispirited people. However, if we use an objective attitude to conduct a fair review, all the grand and enthusiastic movements mostly only had temporary excitement and failed to achieve universal and practical results, lacking sincerity. This is not my personal subjective assertion, but a historical lesson that everyone who truly cares about the country should jointly bear.

The New Life Movement is, of course, a movement to transform the nation and revive the people. (See my book, "National Revival and Transformation of People's Lives," Chen Bao, 23, 11, 21.) But if we want to realize its such a great mission, we must first avoid falling into the past failures of all national salvation movements, thoroughly eliminate those corrupt elements who are realistic, opportunistic, double-dealing, deceiving the world and stealing fame, and whose words do not match their actions. If the New Life Movement is destroyed and dies out by these corrupt elements, it is better to temporarily "my way does not prevail" than to let them deceive the world with grand words and lose credibility with the people. Losing credibility with the people is the most dangerous thing in politics. The reason why the Chinese people are not interested in politics or other public affairs and are unwilling to be serious, although it is because political education is not developed, is actually a problem worth considering. If we want to promote government orders and stimulate the people's interest in politics, we should first "show the people faith." Otherwise, any movement will only drive the masses to the wrong path of vanity, pride, and meanness, and our great and pure nation will only become increasingly degenerate. I, personally, dare to say that I have always been a practitioner of the New Life Movement. Of course, I am extremely unwilling for my words to unfortunately come true, and especially because the life of the nation is already so critical, we cannot afford to make the same mistake again and again, making this movement, which bears the important mission of recreating the life of the nation, take the same old path. Therefore, with my full enthusiasm, I put forward the following three minimum hopes that should be achieved:

1. I hope that in the future, every practitioner of the New Life Movement will try to avoid hypocrisy, show sincerity, match words with actions, and practice what they preach.

2. I hope that people from all walks of life will unanimously and thoroughly understand right and wrong and uphold justice, because only in a society where right and wrong are clear and justice is upheld will everyone be willing to abide by etiquette and righteousness, and be able to understand integrity and shame.

3. I hope that the government authorities will thoroughly and strictly define rewards and punishments, revitalize discipline, and eliminate corruption, because only in a country where rewards and punishments are clear, corruption is eliminated, and discipline is revitalized will society have right and wrong, justice, and the people will understand etiquette and righteousness, know integrity and shame, have discipline, and observe order. Otherwise, in a deformed society where good people are always at a disadvantage, who would be willing to restrain themselves and be good? (See my book, "The Life Movement and Political Reform," Chen Bao New Year's Day Special Issue.)

The above three hopes are theoretically very ordinary, but practically the most important. As long as they are known and can be acted upon, practice is not difficult. In the future, our government and people must truthfully and genuinely practice these three points in a down-to-earth manner, and China's politics, society, and people's hearts will have the possibility and reality of thorough transformation, and our Chinese nation will have the hope of revival. Written at Zilijai in Shanghai on the first anniversary of the New Life Movement, 1935.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 159

— (Xu Xiaoting)

Society is cold and ruthless, and people's hearts are frozen. Whether it is a fallen comrade or a poor friend who has lost economic autonomy, in modern society, if you ask for help, it is like a goat begging for mercy from a hungry tiger. You cannot get warmth and sympathy.

Although the King of Hell is spit out of the mouths of Taoist women and is the authority who holds the power of life and death, the authority of bandits in the countryside is even more absolute than that of the King of Hell.

If there are no evil people in the world, society can be peaceful. If there are no mediocre people in the world, the country can be strong. If there are no idle people in the world, the local area can be prosperous.

Prohibition and Promotion 160

— Shi Didi

In the past year or two, in various vibrant cities, a floor-length gown can be seen on those beautiful women. As high heels step with a rhythmic sound, this soft corner of the dress waves, showing an even more graceful demeanor. It is said that the popularity of long clothes also has a very twisted experience. A few years ago, the silk merchants of Paris, in order to deal with the surplus of their own goods, devised a way to contact fashionable seamstresses, turning light short dresses into flowing long dresses. When women had to lift their skirts and move slowly, the silk merchants' products gained full sales. I remember last summer, not wearing socks was temporarily popular among fashionable women, and the sock industry was deeply affected. Our merchants also came up with some clever methods, unanimously requesting the government to prohibit bare feet, in order to correct the declining morals and maintain commerce. But it had little effect. The methods of these Paris silk merchants, whether ingenious or not, are truly incomparable.

Today, women's every move is subject to strict restrictions, as if social unrest, economic decline, and all the unfortunate events that occur are caused by women's novel costumes and attractive smiles. So, a lot of voices of prohibition came. Prohibiting the wearing of floor-dragging cheongsams, prohibiting female students from applying rouge and powder, and prohibiting other things, really makes people dizzy and at a loss. These complex prohibitions are really not easy to understand clearly, and it is somewhat dangerous to be careless. However, perhaps because most women do not and do not want to understand the reasons for those prohibitions, they still apply powder, still apply rouge, and the floor-dragging gowns have not been shortened by even a fraction of an inch. This exactly matches the saying that women are irrational creatures.

Yes, those glamorous clothes and eye-catching jewelry not only exacerbate the decadence of the end of the century but also send tens of millions of dollars to other countries, without gaining anything practical, except to hasten their own race to the road of destruction. Prohibition, no matter how strict, is justified and cannot be criticized. However, we have heard that for the handling of everything, prohibition only belongs to the negative end. Here, we might as well learn the methods of the silk merchants, using the only common ailment of the women's world—the trend of fashion—to mobilize those famous boudoir beauties, noblewomen, red film stars, and singers and dancers, as long as they are figures that the women's world pays attention to, to rise up and set an example, creating a new fashion. At that time, there will be no need for prohibition, no need for strict orders, and they will obediently follow another path.

Record of Foreign Pigs Coming to China 161

— Kang Jianzhaifu

Wuxi Educational College and the Agricultural College of Zhongda jointly ordered twenty-one high-quality pigs from the United States at the end of last year, which arrived in Shanghai by the ×× President a few days ago. The college specially dispatched a "commissioner" to welcome and pick them up, transferred them to the Beijing-Shanghai train, and arrived at the Wuxi station, where they were transferred to rickshaws to be pulled away. Unexpectedly, one of them escaped from its cage midway and ran into a blacksmith's shop. That day was the eve of the Lunar New Year's Eve. The shop owner thought that a live pig entering the door was very unlucky and refused to let it go. The commissioner got out of the car to negotiate, and after the police persuaded him, the conditions were agreed: the Educational College would send someone to the pig's place to burn a "six-eyed" pig head the next day to return the profit, guaranteed by the Public Security Bureau.

In order to win over the public and welcome back the foreign pigs, the Educational College immediately sent a farmer from the college the next day with a small pig's head, a skinny chicken, a four-inch-long carp, a string of yuanbao, three loud sounds of "Shang Sheng," and five hundred firecrackers to the pig's blacksmith shop to fulfill the treaty. The foreign pig was then happily carried back.

It is said that each foreign pig cost about 25 US dollars, and the freight cost about 20 US dollars per pig, plus other miscellaneous expenses. Each pig costs 160 Chinese yuan. That kind of pig has a particularly strong growth force. Four months after birth, the largest has grown to 165 pounds. This pig is called Chester White and has white fur all over its body. Another kind is called Poland China, which is a mixed breed of Middle and Poland, with mostly black and little white fur. The most peculiar is Duroc Jersey, whose coat is pure yellow. Because the name is quite difficult to remember, it is jokingly translated as "university professor."
