Occasional Notes 163

— (Wang Canying)

A pair of feet from east to west;

Dimples that smile north and south!

Charlie Chaplin, the American silver screen star, has those particularly peculiar feet, whose gait is extremely comical. In Hefei city, Anhui, I often saw a man, about forty years old, who was a dwarf, but not extremely so; his feet were also like Chaplin's, turned outwards to the left and right, forming a straight line, and his gait, without any learning, was naturally amusing! However, Chaplin's is fake; this one is real. If the film industry could discover him, he would be a treasure!

Ms. Hu Die, the silver screen star of Shanghai, has a dimple on her "left cheek," and she is beautiful, needless to say—have you gentlemen been to Tianjin and Beijing? Do you remember Ms. Wang Fengyong, who sings Xihe Dagu (a type of storytelling with drum accompaniment)? Her voice, lingering and unbroken, truly surpasses the Shandong Li Hua Pian (a type of folk opera), and I fear that even the Black Girl and White Girl that Lao Can praised in the Baotu Spring were not her equal! She is also most beautiful, with a dimple on her "right cheek." She is from Yixian, Hebei, and often says, "The mountains and waters of western Beijing are comparable to those of the southeast." It is not surprising that beautiful women are produced there, but it is truly unique and rare that she can be paired with Ms. Hu Die, one left and one right, forming north and south smiling dimples!

Little Western Paradise 164

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Unskilled in Flattery, Seeking Help Meets Scolding; Unable to Return, Led Astray by Exaggerated Praise from a Guest

The waiter glanced at the Hu mother and daughter and smiled at him: "It's rare to see Mr. Zhang being so enthusiastic." Having said that, he smiled and left. Zhang Jiefu knew very well that the waiter had misunderstood, but whether he acted as a matchmaker for Cheng Shengqian or for Chief Gao, it would not harm his own status. After the waiter left, he originally wanted to go back to the window of the Western restaurant to take a look. However, with these two poor women in the room, there were many things scattered about, which was not very appropriate. Therefore, he suppressed his impulse and did not leave, but chatted idly with Mrs. Hu. Mrs. Hu was surprised that this old man was so talkative and jovial, and she was very happy. After talking for about ten minutes, the waiter had not returned with a reply, and he stretched his head to look outside the door, but there was no sign of him. It was just the front and back yards from here to the hall, why was it taking so long? Thinking of this suspicious point, he put his hands behind his back and paced back and forth in the room, trying to reduce the frustration in his heart. However, after walking back and forth four or five times, he felt frustrated again, thinking, "Even if poor people are reliable, if I go out, I will only be standing in the yard. A woman who has just come to a big city would not have the nerve to take things from the room casually. Even if they did take something, they are so thin that they would not be able to hide it anywhere. In that case, I should be bold and go out to take a look." Thinking this way, he decided to walk to the window of the back wall of the Western restaurant. When he looked inside, Cheng Shengqian was talking to a man in a Western suit on one side. Jiefu did not recognize the director of construction here, and thought to himself, "Could this man in the Western suit be him?" So he quietly moved his feet, flashed to the side of the window, and stuck half of his face out to look inside the window. He saw the man in the Western suit frowning and smiling bitterly, and though he was saying something, it was not audible because his voice was soft. (136)

Fragrant Shadows of the Imperial Incense Burner 165

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Once the program was decided, someone went down to prepare.

All the equipment for performing operas was purchased very completely in the palace, and people managed it very carefully, so it was not difficult to get what was needed when it was time to use it. All the backdrops, costumes, and so on were exquisite, and appropriate attire was available for spring, summer, autumn, and winter. Those who hear these words may not be able to fully believe them, thinking that this is very impossible in fact; however, it is true! All day long, all year round, they were always tailoring costumes or sending well-made designs to Suzhou or Guangdong to be custom-made, always sparing no expense. Although they had not come east with us this time, we had already loaded all kinds of things used for performing operas from the carriage, leaving nothing out. Just taking care of this item, such as musical instruments, was the responsibility of an old eunuch, who had a dozen or twenty young eunuchs as assistants. So no matter what opera we performed, as long as we ordered it, we could always put it on. Half of the reason was the completeness of the attire, but the biggest reason was that the eunuchs who performed the operas, whether they were male roles, female roles, painted-face roles, or clowns, could all sing many operas and could be put together at any time without any roles missing.

To perform an opera, there must be a stage. Fortunately, although the buildings of these palaces in Shengjing were very old, there was a stage built in the open space in front of a grand hall. Of course, its age was also very old! The format was the same as the stages we usually see in temples, only one story high, but the location was relatively spacious. (247)

Short Story

Debt 166

— Pan Zhaogan

It was a winter midnight. The headwind howled against his body, as if ten thousand sharp needles were pricking him. White snow covered the earth, and the beautiful village had become a pure white color. Because of the reflection of the light, when viewed from afar, it looked like a piece of uneven glass.

At this time, the people of the whole village had quietly gone to seek their sweet dreams. At the end of the small bridge, on the paper window of a birdcage-like hut made of straw, a faint light flickered.

An old woman over sixty years old lay on a broken plank bed, covered with a broken cotton quilt, unable to resist the invasion of the severe cold, constantly shivering, her face pale and frightening, but as if she were looking forward to something.

"Mother... Mother... I'm back." Accompanied by this weak voice, a beautiful girl, about twenty years old, came in.

"How... was it today?" The old woman struggled to say on the bed.

"Alas! Today" It's cold, and most of the customers are shrinking back and not happy to come out. I only got two dollars, how can I afford to hire a doctor and buy medicine? There's no rice for tomorrow either, alas! As she spoke, she sighed and brushed the snow off her body.

"............" There was silence for a while.

"Hey, hey, is Xiaozhen back?" Suddenly an old man walked in, his face showing a cunning look.

"Um! I'm back." "Fourth Master!" Xiaozhen said, her voice trembling severely.

"Haha! How's the money? The money!"

"I'm really very sorry. Fourth Master, please come and get it tomorrow!"

"Hey! That's not possible, I must have it today."

Xiaozhen's frostbitten face suddenly turned gray. She handed the two dollars that she had planned to use for medical expenses to Fourth Master tremblingly.

"Um! Good, you really don't know how to appreciate favors!" Fourth Master took the money and strode away, muttering in his mouth.

"Mother, the money is gone, what should we do? Oh! How about this! Let's borrow money from Uncle Cheng."

At this time, the old woman had fallen asleep, her face paler than before, and her body was constantly shivering.

Xiaozhen waited for her to stop responding and ran out quickly.

In the end, Xiaozhen couldn't withstand the severe cold and succumbed to the northwest wind. She returned to the house. She thought there was half a loaf of bread left over from yesterday that could be used to fill her mother's stomach and ward off the cold.

She walked into the kitchen, wanting to boil tea to drink, and when she saw that her mother was not breathing, she quickly threw down the bread, ran to the bed, and stood there stunned. After a long time, she cried "Mom:" and fainted.

The northwest wind was still blowing outside, and everything, everything, was still the same as before, only there was a faint and continuous sound coming from inside the house.

"Mother... Mother... how could you bear to abandon your poor daughter... and leave alone?"

Special Issue Commemorating the Anniversary of the New Life Movement

The New Line of the New Life Movement 167

— Wu Tiecheng

Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek initiated the New Life Movement in Nanchang last year, the whole country has followed suit, and people at home and abroad have responded enthusiastically! As a result, it has developed into a movement, forming a trend. All people of insight regard this as a great step forward in the national revival movement. Even foreigners who spy on our country cannot help but admire and sigh, believing that the rise and fall of the new China depends solely on the success or failure of the New Life Movement! In this day and age, if one does not change current customs, it is impossible for the country not to perish! Tracing back to the late Qing Dynasty, when the doors were opened and the country was beset by internal and external troubles, the shortcomings of the nation were fully exposed. Zeng Guofan and Li Hongzhang were shocked by the strong armor and sharp weapons of the powers. Therefore, they sent students and competed to manufacture things, thinking of using the knowledge of sound, light, electricity, and chemistry to continue the decline and restore the country. However, merely relying on the imitation of technology could not help to renew the national policy! Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao took advantage of this and launched the Reform Movement, hoping to adopt the dross of constitutional government from the Eastern neighbor as the model for reform in China. This was putting the cart before the horse! Sun Yat-sen, the leader of our party, was able to perceive the hidden and understand the subtle, with great wisdom and profound thinking, and took the Three Principles of the People as the guideline for revolution and national construction. In recent years, although worries and disasters have arisen repeatedly, and there has been internal turmoil, the central government has been consolidated, the political situation has remained unchanged, and the great cause of national unity and national revival has already begun. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, seeing that the founding and independence of the country depend on the rise of the people, again advocated the New Life Movement, to practice the virtues of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame in the daily life of clothing, food, housing, and transportation, so that everyone understands propriety, righteousness, knows integrity and shame, takes responsibility, and obeys discipline. This is his painstaking effort to awaken the deaf and enlighten the foolish, which is enough to rectify customs, establish national norms, and open historical records. Who would say it is inappropriate!

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek explained the New Life Movement, saying: "The New Life Movement is a revolution in the life of all our people." He explained the meaning of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, saying: "Propriety is order; it is an attitude of being well-behaved. Righteousness is suitability; it is a righteous behavior. Integrity is clarity; it is a clear distinction between right and wrong. Shame is knowledge; it is a sincere awareness." He also said: "Shame is the motive of behavior, integrity is the guide of behavior, righteousness is the practice of behavior, and propriety is the expression of behavior. The four are interconnected; they originate from shame, are clarified by integrity, are practiced in righteousness, and are expressed in propriety. They need each other and complement each other, and none can be missing!" All of these are subtle words and profound meanings, and have already been understood by the whole country! I, Tiecheng, am not clever, and I want to do my best to offer my humble opinion, in order to seek correction from my comrades and compatriots, that is, the new line of the New Life Movement.

From a historical perspective, the Chinese nation is indeed a great and excellent nation. However, in the past hundred years, accumulated habits have been passed down, and there are indeed undeniable weaknesses. In terms of public life, there is no organization, no discipline, and no responsibility. In terms of private life, there is no organization, no discipline, and no responsibility. The lower classes are ignorant and unaware of anything besides food and clothing! The upper classes are incompetent and unable to defend, fearful and weak, immersed in writing, and do not engage in production! The habits of collapsing, decaying, indolent, and sluggishness, and the wind of following old ways and stealing ease, have filled the country and become serious disasters! If we want China to stand on its own in this world, then we must thoroughly transform the national life of China, so that it conforms to the meaning of the New Life, and in terms of its line, I believe there are three.

First, the militarization of national life. China, as a cultural nation, has always prided itself on civil affairs. Since the Tang Dynasty, the authorities of successive dynasties, fearing the disasters of separatist warlords, vigorously promoted the policy of promoting civil affairs and suppressing military affairs, and the spirit of strength and vigor was swept away! Civil affairs and military achievements are mutually supportive. Only when civil and military affairs are both prosperous can a nation be fit for survival. If there is only civil affairs and no military affairs, then it is a conquered slave! The Japanese ridiculed our China as "a country of letters!" They even said that Chinese literature is vast and profound, surpassing ancient and modern times, but those who excel in letters are not necessarily strong in force, so once they encounter nomadic tribes from outside the Great Wall, destruction follows. Their words are enough to be a warning. Not only that, but modern warfare is a three-dimensional war, and mobilization is the mobilization of the people. The development of modern weapons and military science is based on a high degree of scientific civilization. If China does not want to perish, then it must correct its historical weaknesses, strive to promote scientific civilization, popularize military knowledge, militarize national life, and make all aspects of clothing, food, housing, and transportation simple, plain, neat, and solemn. In particular, we should strive to popularize physical education and thoroughly militarize the youth. Even civil servants should often receive military training in their spare time, so that peacetime is like wartime, tense and solemn, knowing shame and teaching war, and washing away the historical habits of weakness and decadence of our nation!

Second, the productionization of national life. The economy is the foundation of the country. The rise and fall of a country's politics and the prosperity and decline of a nation all depend on it. In the past, Guan Zhong said: "Travel through the mountains and lakes, observe the mulberry and hemp, and calculate the production of the six domestic animals, and the wealth or poverty of the country can be known." He also said: "If there is more grassland and less cultivated land, even if there is no drought or flood, the country will be hungry. If this is the case and there are few people, it will not be enough to defend its land... If the people are not enough to defend, their cities will not be strong. If the people are hungry, they cannot be used to fight. If the industries are scattered and not defended, then the country will be in ruins!" Guan Zhong lived in an agricultural era, and the relationship between the economy and the national destiny was already like this, let alone today! To talk about developing the economy, production is paramount. The state should do its best to plan construction, control water conservancy, open up transportation, reclaim wasteland, and provide sufficient food for the people; use economic policies to guide industry and commerce, and adjust finance. For the people, every aspect of daily life should be in harmony with the meaning of production, that is, promote cherishing time, pay attention to work efficiency, regard diligence as a social virtue, and regard idleness and sitting idle without working as a deep shame. On the one hand, we should encourage frugality, so that the amount of social consumption does not exceed the amount of social production. In particular, we should promote the national concept of consumption, so that everyone knows that the gathering of buying and consumption, from a thread to a penny to an object, is all related to the rise and fall of national power and the prosperity and decline of the nation. Let compatriots across the country wear Chinese clothes, eat Chinese food, live in Chinese houses, and travel in China. If all the necessities of life can be obtained from domestic products, then the excess of imports over exports can be eliminated and the economic difficulties of the country can be alleviated! If the New Life Movement can do its best to achieve this, then its benefits to the country will be extensive!

Third, the artisticization of national life. The method of the New Life Movement emphasizes persuasion and edification, and does not adopt a coercive command style. If we want to penetrate into the people and transform the people into customs, then promoting the artisticization of national life is essential. Art is what distinguishes civilization from barbarism, and music is what distinguishes order from chaos. Taking music as an example, noble and pure music is enough to cultivate temperament, promote national integrity, console sorrow and resentment, and promote ambition, so that social vitality is abundant and interest in life is doubled. Conversely, if one indulges in the sound of killing and attack and the decadent sound, then it will only lead the people to the realm of licentiousness, and the harm it causes is immeasurable. How well said by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek: "If we start our revolutionary tutelage by promoting music, I think the results will be even more rapid. For example, if a place can set up a school that mainly promotes music, the general public will flock to it, and the effect of transforming the people into customs will definitely be even greater!" If we can take the artisticization of national life as a path, then the New Life Movement will be welcomed by the entire nation, and the magnitude of the results will be obvious. In short, one era has the mission of one era, and one era has the model of one era. China is at the meeting of old and new changes. The old ones have disappeared, and the new ones have not yet been established. The New Life Movement is enough to be the model of this era. The aforementioned lines seem necessary. My humble opinion is like this. I hope that the wise men in the country will correct me!

Shanghai City New Life Movement One Year Work Report 168

— Wu Kaixian

I. The Initiation and Implementation of the New Life Movement

(I) The Initiation of the New Life Movement

The New Life Movement has now spread throughout the country. Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek established the outline, changed the Nanchang New Movement Association to the General Association, hired administrative officials from various provinces and cities to serve as instructors, and promulgated organizational outlines to unify the organization, the steps in various places have become more consistent, and promotion has become more convenient. The New Life Movement in this city was initiated around March of last year, and it was officially reorganized and established in July. The preparation process is described below.

Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek advocated the New Life Movement in February of last year, it has swept across the country. Party, government, and military authorities in this city believed that this movement was critical to the rise and fall of the nation and should be promoted. After a joint meeting, it was decided to start preparations on March 20 at the remaining buildings of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office in Fenglinqiao. A declaration was issued, and initiatives were sought. A total of 315 people joined as initiators, and 300 people as supporters. The drafting of regulations and the compilation and printing of propaganda outlines took only twelve days, which was extremely tight.

(II) Summary of Work Progress

After the preparations were completed, an inaugural meeting was held on April 1. The charter and covenants of the association were approved, and important matters such as holding a propaganda week and experimental areas were resolved. 178 directors and supervisors were elected, and Mayor Wu Tiecheng was elected as the chairman of the board. The organization of the board of directors and supervisors is recorded on the left.

(A) Board of Directors: Composed of 79 directors and 41 alternate directors. At the joint meeting of directors and supervisors on April 5, the directors passed the organizational rules and elected 21 standing directors to form the standing committee. The number of meetings held was: the first on April 5 (immediately after the joint meeting), the second on April 16, and the third on July 24. The important motions of each meeting, in addition to the formulation of general rules for the organization of branches, are detailed in the meeting minutes. The board of directors is divided into the following four groups, each with two directors and deputy directors, and a number of staff members.

(1) General Affairs Group: Director Wu Kaixian, Deputy Director Jiang Huaishu. In addition to handling the daily routine of general affairs, its work also assists all groups in all matters.

(2) Organization Group: Director Wu Xingya, Deputy Director Lu Jingshi. Its work includes organizing branches in various agencies, groups, and schools in the urban area. Twenty-five have been approved for establishment, with more than 8,800 members. There are quite a few that have not been approved for establishment.

(3) Propaganda Group: Director Jun Xingbai, Deputy Director Zheng Zhengqiu. Its work included printing and distributing 50,000 slogans and leaflets, and printing 120,000 copies of booklets such as the Covenant Outline Movement. From April 9 to 15, a propaganda week was held for all sectors of society. Ten thousand people participated in the lantern parade on the 7th, which was a great success for a time. Japanese mail to and from this port was stamped with a special New Life Movement stamp as a memorial. During this week, the film industry publicly screened New Life slogans, and the broadcasting station broadcast the New Life Covenant, giving the citizens of the city a deep impression of the meaning of the New Life Movement.

(4) Guidance Group: Director Pan Gongzhan, Deputy Director Wen Hongen. Its work, in addition to guiding the establishment of various branches, also organized 500 persuasion teams from all walks of life, which were reviewed at the public stadium on June 4. They were neatly dressed and in high spirits. After the review, they immediately set off to persuade pedestrians on the streets.

(B) Board of Supervisors: Composed of 41 supervisors and 17 alternate supervisors. At the joint meeting of directors and supervisors on April 5, the supervisors passed the organizational rules and elected 11 standing supervisors to form the standing committee. The number of meetings held was: the first on April 11, the second on April 25, the third on May 9, the fourth on June 13, and the fifth on July 13. The important motions of each meeting are detailed in the meeting minutes. As for the meeting of the entire board of supervisors, the item was a discussion meeting on April 15. The first meeting of the board of supervisors was on May 9, and the second meeting of the board of supervisors was on July 13. The important motions of each meeting, in addition to the adoption of procedural rules, are also detailed in the meeting minutes. Only one secretary was appointed in the meeting, with Mo Xuanyuan, a standing supervisor, concurrently serving. The staff members were concurrently held by the staff members of the board of directors.

II. Unification and Progress of the New Life Movement

(I) Reorganization and Establishment of the New Life Movement Promotion Association

In early July, the Association received Notice No. 1 from the Nanchang General Association of Chiang Kai-shek, instructing it to reorganize in accordance with the organizational outline promulgated by the General Association. At the same time, Chairman Chiang hired Wu Tiecheng, the chairman of the board, as the instructor of this city, and instructed him to guide the reorganization of the Association. After discussion, it was decided to reorganize in accordance with the order, and all boards of directors and supervisors were terminated. In accordance with the new rules, nine executives were selected from various agencies and groups: Yu Hongjun from the Municipal Government, Wu Kaixian from the Municipal Party Department, Wu Xingya from the Social Affairs Bureau, Pan Gongzhan from the Education Bureau, Wen Hongen from the Public Security Bureau, Yang Hu from the military, Zhang Shouyong from the academic community, Lu Jingshi from the industrial community, and Yu Zuoting from the business community. They were immediately assigned duties and reported to the General Association for record. Looking back from the reorganization to the present, it has been almost July. The circumstances of the successive executive meetings in the past seven months are briefly described below:

The first executive meeting was held on July 30. There were four resolutions. The important ones were the division of labor: Wu Xingya, Yang Hu, and Pan Gongzhan were publicly elected as standing executives, Wu Kaixian as secretary, Lu Jingshi as director of the investigation section, Zhang Shouyong as director of the design section, and Wen Hongen as director of the promotion section.

The second executive meeting was held on August 16. There were three resolutions, the important one being the adoption of the revised charter.

The third executive meeting was held on October 24. There were four resolutions. The important ones were the adoption of measures to reform etiquette and customs, and the adoption of the first phase of the work plan.

The fourth executive meeting was held on December 28. Seven resolutions were discussed. The important ones were: Executive Wen Hongen passed away due to illness, and Director Wen Chaoji of the Bureau was appointed as an executive and director of the promotion section; and the organizational rules of the city's youth service corps were revised and the implementation of new life measures was urged.

The fifth executive meeting was held on February 9 of this year. There were seven resolutions. The important ones were: hiring branch leaders for the youth service corps and adding deputy branch leaders; Executive Wu Kaixian was reassigned as a concurrent standing member and was designated by the instructor as the chief executive, and Executive Pan Gongzhan was reassigned as a concurrent secretary; and a representative conference from all walks of life was held on February 19, the New Life Memorial Day.

(II) Implementation of the Work Plan

The above summary of the situation since the preparation, establishment, reorganization, and current progress can be seen in general. Others, such as the establishment of the Experimental Area Design Committee, and the election of committee members Yu Hongjun, Tao Baichuan, Ding Mocun, Yang Weiyu, and Tai Shuangqiu, were all generated during the previous joint meeting of directors and supervisors. The experimental site was planned to be in Jiangwan or Wusong, and it has been discussed and progressed through numerous meetings. However, due to tight funding, it has not been realized. The current planned progress is (1) urging and examining the implementation of new life by staff members of various agencies, (2) urging and examining the implementation of new life in various public places (such as restaurants and hotels), (3) compiling various cost-effective art slogans on carriages and thoroughfares, guiding the methods, and (4) rectifying the city appearance, etc., and regulations and measures have been drafted and implemented separately.

III. Main Tasks of the New Life Movement in the Future

(I) Propaganda: To hope that the public understands and recognizes the true meaning of the New Life Movement, it depends on extensive and in-depth propaganda. The propaganda work of the Association, in addition to the above-mentioned printing and distribution of slogans and booklets, and the holding of propaganda weeks and large lantern parades, still needs to be continued due to the vast area and dense population, so that everyone knows it. Therefore, the planned activities for this year are to establish permanent slogans. Choose key thoroughfares and make neon lights and large oil paint slogans with artistic methods and thought-provoking words to inspire deep thought. In addition, public vehicles and ships, which have a large number of passengers every day, have also been carefully considered.

(II) Supervision: The implementation of the New Life Movement cannot be neglected, and this supervision must be slightly compulsory when necessary to achieve results. The planned supervision work for this year is to start with various agencies and their staff. Monthly reflection forms and instructions on how to work from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek will be issued, and they will be asked to sign and recognize them, and they will be assessed at any time. The New Life Movement in public places must also be carried out at the same time. Regarding various regulations, they have all been drafted and can be distributed to various public places for implementation in accordance with the regulations. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau will conduct inspections and crackdowns at any time, which should be effective.

(III) Persuasion: The implementation of the New Life Movement in public places can be compulsory due to their business nature, but the implementation of the New Life Movement in households depends on persuasion in addition to supervision. Regarding this matter, the Association has also planned measures to organize youth service corps, adopting a branch system, and soliciting party members, students from various schools, boy scouts, etc. to serve as members in each area, taking turns to serve. On weekends and holidays, they will go to thoroughfares and streets to guide pedestrians and households to implement the New Life Movement on the spot. Those who unreasonably resist will be required to ask the police officers of the Public Security Bureau to take them to the scene to reprimand them.

It should also be mentioned that the environment of this city is different due to the relationship of the concession, and the promotion of the New Life Movement has not been as expected. Therefore, the established plan can only be guided by the situation and gradually progressed. It is hoped that wise men from all walks of life will always give guidance, and the business funds will be determined as soon as possible, so that the efforts to promote and realize the plan, and the future of the New Life Movement, will depend on it.

Promotion of the New Life Movement 169

— Pan Gongzhan

The New Life Movement has been initiated and advocated by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Nanchang for a year now. In the past year, various places have responded successively, and there have been quite a few New Life Movement Promotion Associations established one after another. This city is a major port in the southeast, and the world's attention is focused on it. The promotion of the New Life Movement should not be delayed. However, looking back at the past achievements, the scope has not been expanded sufficiently, and the public has not universally practiced it. The decadent and dissolute life remains the same. Perhaps this is also because those who practice the New Life have failed to widely advise with their experience and spread it as a trend? The past time cannot be recovered, and the future movement must be redoubled. I believe that those who practice the New Life must pay attention to the following ways of promotion:

1. From shallow to deep: The promotion of the New Life Movement hopes that the behavior of the people across the country conforms to propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, and is expressed in various daily lives such as clothing, food, housing, and transportation. However, the realization of the above goals is not achieved overnight. It should be from shallow to deep, first the simple and then the heavy, and it must not be interrupted, and progress step by step to achieve the artistic and rationalization of life, and adapt to the needs of the times and the environment.

2. From near to far: The New Life Movement is not a matter for one person, but a matter for the common efforts of the entire nation. Like a machine, if you want it to run quickly and increase its efficiency, any part cannot lose its function. Those who practice the New Life should take the sincerity of pushing oneself and others, from one person to one family, from family to neighborhood and village, from near to far, the scope will expand day by day, and the practitioners will gradually increase, so that the lives of the people across the country will be renewed, and everyone will be a healthy citizen.

3. Persistent: The achievement of any career is not determined by the enthusiasm of the moment, but by the perseverance to practice it persistently. Therefore, the word "persistence" is the mother of success. When the New Life Movement is advocated by everyone, it will inevitably be vigorous and diligent in practice. Once the time has passed, it often returns to its original appearance, and the various rules of the New Life are left behind. Therefore, practitioners must be persistent, first create good habits, and after a long time, they will settle in this kind of life and not feel it.

Now the national situation is critical, and it is the critical moment for the survival of the Chinese nation. The success or failure of the New Life Movement is what the national spirit strikes. Guanzi said that propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are the four dimensions of the country. If the four dimensions are not expanded, the country will perish. If most people do not know what propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are, then they will inevitably not distinguish between right and wrong, not examine public and private affairs, not understand the root and the branch, and take interest inappropriately. Young people are dissolute and extravagant, and adults are昏庸corrupt. The rich are engaged in frivolity, and the poor fall into meanness. It is very difficult to hope that such an unorganized, undisciplined, and immoral people can survive in modern times. The New Life Movement, on the surface, is only to make personal life conform to the rules, and its ultimate goal is to relate to the survival of the nation. Therefore, the New Life Movement is a self-reliance movement of our nation, a life revolution of our nation, and a renaissance movement of the nation. Those of us who have the responsibility to promote the New Life Movement must understand this meaning together, and then we can make the greatest determination, jointly abide by it, and widely advise it, to save the now endangered nation.

Further New Life Movement 170

— Tao Baichuan

Written for the Anniversary of the New Life Movement

I. Further on the Anniversary

Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek advocated the New Life Movement on February 19 last year, everyone has believed that this is the starting point of the Chinese people's life revolution and the basic work of reviving the Chinese nation. Therefore, the upper echelons influenced the lower echelons, and it was a fad for a while. Time flies, and now it is the anniversary.

The guiding principles of the New Life Movement are propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame. To achieve these principles, the first priority is "rules" and "cleanliness." Rules and cleanliness are certainly good goals, but these two alone cannot achieve the purpose of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame. Therefore, we hope that Chairman Chiang can put forward slightly higher goals and make a "further New Life Movement."

Sure enough, Chairman Chiang has recently told us: "Rules and cleanliness are only the beginning of this movement, that is, the lowest target of this movement. After the anniversary, we plan to maintain and enrich the past achievements on the one hand, and promote further on the other hand, that is, the national people's 'life militarization,' 'life productionization,' and 'life artification' that we plan."

From rules and cleanliness to life militarization, productionization, and artification, this is a "further New Life Movement."

II. Life Militarization

Regarding life militarization, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek said: "It is not intended to arm the people of the whole country at the same time and go to the border; in the initial stage, it is only to expect them to be strict in organization, value unity, abide by discipline, pay attention to order, be energetic, maintain solemnity, and wash away the previous habits of disorganization, romance, following the old ways, and苟安," and the main points are as follows:

1. Salute when raising and lowering the national flag.

2. Stand up when the party song is played.

3. Support the leader.

4. Obey the discipline.

5. Everyone must receive military training.

6. Everyone must receive civic training.

7. Implement air defense exercises.

8. Implement rescue exercises.

9. Walk on the left.

10. Keep your eyes level and your head up when walking.

11. Take less cars and walk more.

12. The utensils should be simple.

13. Get up early and go to bed early.

14. Exercise every day.

III. Life Productionization

Regarding life productionization, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek said: "It is not intended to make all the people in the country be farmers, workers, or merchants. In the initial stage, it is only to expect them to be able to save, be diligent, care about the difficulty of material resources, and devote themselves to the path of production, and wash away the previous habits of extravagance, waste, enjoyment, and leisure." The main points are as follows:

1. Labor.

2. Use domestic products.

3. Save expenses.

4. Reduce socializing.

5. Everyone joins the cooperative.

6. Reclaim wasteland and plant trees.

7. Work hard on family handicrafts.

8. No prostitution, no gambling, no smoking, no alcoholism.

9. Money must be saved.

10. Tea and snacks can be used for wedding and funeral banquets.

11. Find something to do when you have nothing to do.

12. Cherish time.

13. Use waste.

IV. Life Artification

Regarding life artification, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek said: "It is not intended to make all the people in the country be writers, elegant scholars, painters, sculptors, and musicians. In the initial stage, it is only to expect them to be polite, humble, clean, tidy, lively, and optimistic, and wash away the previous habits of rudeness, meanness, narrowness, and ignorance." The main points are as follows:

1. Eat cleanly.

2. Dress simply.

3. Keep the residence tidy.

4. Speak truthfully.

5. Act quickly.

6. Be energetic in doing things.

7. Be polite to others.

V. Significance of the Anniversary

The New Life Movement is already an anniversary! The New Life Movement Promotion Association has designated February 19 as the New Life Movement Memorial Day. We want to develop the spirit of "reviewing the past and encouraging the future." Let's thoroughly review our individual lives and actively strive! We also want to go a step further, from "cleanliness" and "rules" to "life militarization," "life productionization," and "life artification"!

(Northeast News Agency) After the fall of the Northeast, the Japanese have become more and more aggressive in cultural aggression, and forced the Puppet Ministry of Education to accept their enslaving education policy and implement it in schools in the Northeast to anesthetize young students. As for the qualification examinations for middle school principals, they will be conducted separately after the teacher qualification examinations. The exam papers have been reviewed, and a total of 19 students studying in specialized schools in Japan, 62 students studying in higher specialized schools, and 11 students studying in middle schools have been admitted. There are a total of 92 students studying in Japan.

Puppet New East Library

(Changchun News) The Puppet New Capital Library has added a large number of books on friendship between Japan and "Manchukuo" and other anesthetic books since January 1 this year. The content of these books is mostly materials such as the loyalty to the emperor and patriotism unilaterally promoted by the Japanese puppets.

The Two Ministries of Education Submit a Request to Stipulate Children's Year 177

From April 12 of this year to April 3 of next year (Nanjing, 18th) The two Ministries of Education presented to the Executive Yuan on the 18th, in order to arouse the attention of the national people to children's education, protect children's physical and mental health, and seek children's welfare, so as to complete the physical, mental, and social abilities of children, please stipulate that from April 12 of this year to April 3 of the next year will be the National Children's Year. The implementation measures are: the central government will be in charge of the implementation committee of the National Children's Year jointly organized by the two Ministries of Education and the Ministry of Education. Each province will be in charge of the implementation committee of the National Children's Year jointly organized by the two halls of education and civil affairs and the labor administrative organs, and the children's business groups. The special city has a social affairs bureau jointly organized by the education administrative and health administrative organs, and the children's business groups, which are respectively organized by the provincial and municipal children's year implementation committees. The county and city governments will meet with the relevant organs, and the children's business groups will organize the county and city children's year implementation committees. The Central Party Department will be ordered by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to assist the various levels of the Party Department. The National Children's Year Implementation Committee will be established this month and will end in June next year. The detailed implementation measures will be announced after being approved by the Executive Yuan.

Record of the Official Establishment of the Board of Directors of the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society 180

Chen Qicai Elected as Chairman of the Board

And Discussed Matters Concerning the Improvement of Society Affairs

The Chinese Arts and Crafts Society held a general meeting for the establishment of the board of directors on the 16th of this month at the Tung Chi University Alumni Association in Nanjing. The election of the chairman and the discussion of various improvement proposals were as follows:

Directors Present The directors present on this day included Chen Qicai, Chen Daqi, Ma Zongrong, Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan (represented by Liu Baimin), Chen Lifu, Wu Zhihui (represented by He Bingsong), Chuan Shi Shuo, Hu Shuhua, Wang Yunwu, Zhou Changshou, He Bingsong, Wang Shijie, Zheng Zhenwen, and more than ten others. He Bingsong was publicly elected as the temporary chairman, and Liu Baimin as the temporary secretary. Election of Chairman After the report, the chairman was elected according to the regulations. Wang Shijie and Ma Zongrong counted the ballots. As a result of the ballot count, Chen Qicai was elected as the chairman, Chuan Shi Shuo and Chen Daqi were elected as supervisors of the fund, and Pan Gongzhan was elected as the secretary. After taking office, discussions were held on various proposals such as preparing for the establishment of a National Music Research Institute, compiling a series of national rejuvenation books, enriching the Arts and Crafts Library, and improving the Arts and Crafts Middle School. It was decided to actively proceed with these proposals. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Upon Returning to Shanghai The president of the society, He Bingsong, as well as Chuan Shi Shuo, Zhou Changshou, Liu Baimin, and others returned to Shanghai by train that evening. In addition to reporting the situation in Nanjing to the directors in Shanghai, they will also convene a board meeting, it is said.

Chinese Agronomy Society Commemorates the Late Director Xu Shuji 181

Mr. Xu Shuji, Director of the Chinese Agronomy Society, has served as the society's Secretary-General, Director-General, and Chairman for more than ten years, presiding over the society's affairs with enthusiasm. The society's foundation has been strengthened, and its reputation has spread throughout the country, all thanks to Mr. Xu's planning and strategies. In October of last year, Director Xu also authored the book "The Food Problem" in the Agricultural Studies Series for the society. Shortly after the manuscript was completed, he unfortunately passed away at his residence in Peiping on November 9 due to overwork. The agricultural community was saddened by this news. In accordance with the decision of the board of directors, the society held a memorial service at the society's headquarters in Peiping on February 17. More than 500 mourning couplets and poems were received. In addition to all the directors, members in Peiping and other places also attended. At 2:00 PM, all the members present offered public sacrifices, presided over by the society's current Director Liang Xi. The ceremony was extremely solemn. Members arrived one after another to pay their respects. A total of about 300 people attended until the closing of the meeting at 5:00 PM, it is said.

Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center to Move to Nanjing Tomorrow 184

Personnel Have Been Assigned to Contact the Railway Bureau to Arrange for Transportation

A Small Number of Staff Will Remain in Shanghai to Purchase Books

The new building of the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center in this city, which was built next to the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in Nanjing last year, has been completely completed. The center is scheduled to move to Nanjing starting tomorrow and will open in Nanjing on the 26th. The details are as follows:

The New Building Is Grand The Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center on Foch Road in this city, in view of the development of its business and the expiration of the lease on the original site, raised funds last year by the director of the center, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, and others, to build a general center next to the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in the capital. It has now been completely completed. The three-story building is quite solemn and grand. The center is scheduled to begin moving tomorrow. The city originally intended to set up a distribution office, but this intention has now been abandoned. It has been decided to set up a distribution office in Nanjing instead.

Opening for Business in Nanjing The center was originally divided into three departments: research, publishing, and library. Recently, staff from these three departments, together with staff from the director-general's office, have been sorting out books and documents, assigning numbers, and sending personnel to contact the two railway lines to prepare five train cars to transport furniture and books. The loading will begin tomorrow, and all staff will then take the train to Nanjing, with each person receiving a travel allowance of 20 yuan from the center. The center will be closed for several days during the move. It was originally planned to open for business in Nanjing on March 1, but this has now been changed to the 26th. After the center moves to Nanjing, a portion of the staff will be left in Shanghai to specialize in purchasing books, it is said.

Arriving in Shanghai on the 6th of Next Month

Mr. Chen Heqin, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Chinese Education Department, was granted an eight-month leave by the Municipal Council in July of last year to visit various parts of Europe and the United Kingdom to study educational administration and other matters. Great China University Holds Spring Semester Commencement Ceremony 186

Wang Boqun Speaks on Eight Basic Beliefs

Since the beginning of the semester, new and old students of Great China University have arrived one after another and have already started classes. The spring semester commencement ceremony was held yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, presided over by President Wang Boqun. More than a thousand professors and students attended the meeting. First, President Wang exhorted all students on eight basic beliefs that they should cultivate in the future. Regarding personal cultivation: (1) Strengthen physical fitness and master skills; (2) Advocate thrift and practice integrity; (3) Restrain private desires and strive for public morality; (4) Distinguish right from wrong and uphold justice. Regarding society: (5) Awaken the masses to self-government and self-reliance; (6) Love and help each other and seek happiness together; (7) Unite sincerely and vow to eliminate violence; (8) Revive the nation and save the country from disaster. The audience was deeply moved. Special Feature

Pan Gongzhan's Speech on School Education in Shanghai (1) 188

The fifth lecture in the "Shanghai" system of speeches at the Shanghai YMCA by Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Education Bureau, recorded by Xie Chongshan as follows:

(1)

Chairman, distinguished guests, today the Shanghai YMCA has invited me to speak on the issue of "Education in Shanghai." From my position, currently serving in the administrative affairs of education, I cannot decline this topic due to my responsibilities. However, I do not have the ability to completely explain "Education in Shanghai," and it would be impossible to report everything in detail with statistical figures in such a short period of time. Moreover, I am afraid that everyone would find it troublesome to listen. To be honest, the current educational statistics are not very reliable due to various environmental factors. However, although these statistics may not be completely reliable, they can be used as a rough reference. Therefore, I would like to first make a simple report on the statistics of school education in Shanghai, categorized. After the report, we will discuss these statistics together to see which areas should be emphasized in the future improvement of education in Shanghai.

The Shanghai Municipal Government publishes a statistical book every year, publishing statistical figures for various undertakings such as "Education," "Hygiene," and "Public Security" in Shanghai. However, this is published according to the fiscal year. For example, the statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic of China are from July of the 21st year of the Republic of China to June of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, and the statistics for the 23rd year are from July of the 23rd year to June of the 24th year. Therefore, the statistics I am reporting now are the statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic of China (ending June of the 23rd year). These statistics are currently being printed and will be published soon. However, they are still relatively recent statistics. According to this, the total population of Shanghai is more than 3.4 million, including the scope of the Municipal Government and the Public and French Concessions. How many schools are there in this city with more than 3.4 million people? We will not distinguish between public and private now, but only say the total number of elementary schools, middle schools, and universities. (1) There are 849 elementary schools (including kindergartens, short-term elementary schools, junior elementary schools, and senior elementary schools). There are 137 secondary schools (including junior middle schools, senior middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools). There are 33 higher schools (including vocational schools, independent colleges, and universities). The total number of schools in these three levels of primary, secondary, and higher education is 1,019. (2) Among the schools in the three levels of primary, secondary, and higher education, the number of students is the largest in elementary schools, followed by secondary schools, and then higher schools. There are 158,164 elementary school students, 32,648 secondary school students, and 12,141 higher school students. The total number of students combined is 202,953. (3) In addition to students, we should also pay attention to teachers and staff. There are 6,459 teachers and staff in elementary schools, 3,782 teachers and staff in secondary schools, and 2,363 teachers and staff in higher schools. The total number is 12,604. (4) As for the annual expenses of schools at each level, elementary schools spend 4,111,073 yuan, secondary schools spend 3,926,748 yuan, and higher schools spend 6,436,242 yuan. The total expenditure of all schools is 14,474,063 yuan.

After briefly mentioning the various statistical figures for the 22nd year, we can compare them with the previous year. It can be said that the total figures for each category in the 22nd year have made considerable progress compared to the 21st year. (1) The total number of schools was 967 in the 21st year and 1,019 in the 22nd year, an increase of 52 schools. Among them, the number of elementary schools was 792 in the 21st year and 849 in the 22nd year, an increase of 57 schools, all of which were elementary schools. As for middle schools and universities, there was only a decrease compared to the previous year, with no increase. For example, there were 141 secondary schools in the 21st year and only 137 in the 22nd year, a decrease of 4 schools. There were 34 higher schools in the 21st year, but only 33 in the 22nd year, a decrease of 1 school. (2) Looking at the total number of students, there were 185,661 in the 21st year and 202,953 in the 22nd year, an increase of nearly 20,000 people. Which students increased? Comparing the number of secondary school students with the previous year, there were 29,122 secondary school students in the 21st year and 32,648 in the 22nd year, an increase of more than 3,000 students. What about the number of higher school students? In the 21st year, there were 13,227 higher school students, but only 12,141 in the 22nd year, a decrease of more than 1,000 students. As for the number of elementary school students, there were 143,312 elementary school students in the 21st year and 158,164 in the 22nd year, an increase of almost 15,000 people. Therefore, the increase in students this year was the largest in elementary schools. (3) The expenses of schools at each level are also the same, with more increases in elementary education. The expenses of secondary schools in the 21st year were 3,915,479 yuan, and the expenses in the 22nd year increased to 3,926,748 yuan. The expenses of higher schools in the 21st year were 5,628,596 yuan, and the expenses in the 22nd year increased to 6,436,242 yuan. The expenses of elementary schools in the 21st year were 3,325,421 yuan, and the expenses in the 22nd year increased to 4,111,073 yuan, an increase of almost 800,000 yuan compared with the previous year, while the expenses of middle schools and universities only increased slightly, and the numbers were very small. Therefore, from this simple statistical report, we can get some comparative comfort, that is, from the general situation, although the country is in serious trouble, the social economy is declining, and everyone's livelihood is difficult, under such circumstances, the school education in Shanghai, as a whole, has made considerable progress in the 22nd year compared to the 21st year. Especially gratifying is that the largest part of this progress is in elementary education. The number of elementary schools has increased, the number of students has increased, and the amount of funding has also increased, and the increase is very large. For example, the number of elementary school students has increased to 15,000, and the funding has increased to 800,000 yuan. Compared with the number of students and the amount of funding in secondary and higher education, they have only increased a little, and the numbers are very small. This is a relatively comforting thing.

Why do I only say it is relatively comforting? I personally want to make this clear. This is also a view I have on education in China in the current era, and I cannot help but express it. If my view is correct, then the facts in this report are gratifying. If you think my view is incorrect, then today's report is not a relatively gratifying thing, but even a terrible or painful one. This depends on each person's view on education and their understanding of education, and then decides which point in the current educational view they should pay attention to. (To be continued)

Shanghai Municipal Council's Regulations for Renting Tennis Courts in Two Parks 196

Winter has passed, and the weather is gradually warming up. The tennis season is about to begin. In Hongkou Park and Huishan Park, the Shanghai Municipal Council has specially opened several hard and grass tennis courts. Each year, these are provided to sports enthusiasts for rental. As the sports season is approaching, the council has revised the rental fee regulations to facilitate applications from various sectors. The rental fee regulations and application procedures are listed below:

Rental Fee Regulations: (1) Hard court rental fee per court per season, from May 1st to December 15th: playing all day is $75; playing from 6:00 AM to 9:00 AM is $20; playing from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM is $10; playing from 12:00 PM to 3:00 PM is $15; playing from 3:00 PM until the park closes is $30. Intermediate days are halved. (2) Grass court rental fee from May 15th to September 30th: playing all day is $20; playing on alternate days is $10. (3) Bowling green rental fee per court per day is $5.

Application Procedures: Any group wishing to use the courts may apply to the council. However, they must form an organization, with one person as the representative. The application letter must state: 1. The name of the organization; 2. The name of the chairman or president; 3. The name and address of the secretary; 4. The names of all athletes; 5. The courts requested for use; 6. The number of courts used last year.

The gold market experienced ups and downs yesterday, making it extremely difficult to predict. Page 20

Free Talk

Literary Agent 213

— Zhong Yuan

This is an old tune; in a capitalist society, there is a danger of everything becoming commodified, and thus even literature and art are not spared.

The pinnacle of capitalism is the "Golden Circle Kingdom" of North America. There, the commodification of literature and art is, needless to say, a fact. Of course, this is not to say that everything that belongs to art in the "Golden Circle Kingdom" must be commodified, but rather that there is a great deal of commodified literature and art. For example, war-promoting works that promote sales for arms dealers (or, it doesn't matter if you say American imperialism) are "commodities" that are extremely popular for a time and ostensibly serve the "nation, society," and even "humanity." At worst, there are literary and artistic works for the "leisure" of idle old men, women, young masters, and young ladies. Although they can only be regarded as "luxury goods," they also have a large market.

However, there are also "literary agents" in the literary and art market of the "Golden Circle Kingdom." Speaking of which, the so-called "agent" is honestly a "broker," but the American "literary agent" apparently also has the identity of the "fang guan" in the Chinese imperial examination era. If the "agent" recommends a submission to various magazines and bookstores, there is hope of being used. A "agent" with a good brand has great credibility with any editor. When editors want to find a certain kind of work, they also ask the "agent" to find a way. A "agent" who is doing good business will receive 150 to 160 novels in a week—all waiting to be recommended.

In this way, the works of most unknown American writers first go through the recommendation of an "agent," and then through the selection of the editor, before they can meet the reader.

China is still a backward capitalist country, so although there is commodified "literature," and also commodified "literati," and even more "commercial" "literati," there does not seem to be a formal "literary agent."

However, this is limited to contemporary people and contemporary works. Ancient people and ancient works cannot be used as examples. It seems that China is, after all, an ancient country with 5,000 years of culture. There are as many authors as hair, and as many works as the ocean — just as the editorial department of the "Golden Circle Kingdom" receives an average of 300 manuscripts every day, so there must be "agents." On this point, without Dr. Hu Shih's recommendation, how could "Xingshi Yinyuan" become a "household name?" If it were not for the recommendation of Mr. Lin, how could "Yuan Zhonglang" and others be on the "20% discount" roadside book stalls? Our ancient writers cannot but thank the "agents" of later generations!

However, just as the "agents" of the "Golden Circle Kingdom" "admit that a promising new writer is simply equal to a year of good harvest," we here only discover one or one-and-a-half "promising" ancient literary giants a year. Last year it was Yuan Zhonglang, I wonder who it will be this year?

A Letter from the End of North Sichuan Road 214

— Xiang Yu

Brother Yuanwei!

I haven't had much to report to you for a few months. You have written me letter after letter, so if I don't reply to your letter, it seems a bit unreasonable, so I wrote this letter. In this, you can see that I am fulfilling an obligation, not reporting news. Even if there is some news, it is unimportant. At the same time, what I report may be what you don't want to know, and what you want to know is what I don't want to report. Don't take it as if I'm deliberately arguing with you, I'm just such a strange-tempered person. The more people want me to investigate a certain event on my personal side, the less I want to mention it, and the more people don't want to hear a certain event on my personal side, the more I want to talk about it, so I often answer irrelevant questions. You can already anticipate this result, and I don't need to declare it. Fortunately, I have already said that this is to fulfill an obligation. You can't expect too much from a letter to fulfill an obligation. Naturally, I am again singing a song by Tao Xing, reporting some old clichés. You have already heard these clichés so much that you feel a little annoyed, but what can be done? I'm just that kind of person! Listen carefully, I'm starting to report.

I'm not sick enough to die, as you suspect. You, who care about my health, may be happy to a certain extent about this. However, although I am not dead, I am in a state of neither life nor death, just like you and me together. People have already gotten up in the morning, but I am still lying straight in bed, and people haven't gone to bed at night, but I am already lying straight in bed. I sleep more hours than others, but I sleep less time than others. On moonlit nights, I watch the moon rise to the center, watch the moon set, and watch the sun rise. On windy nights, I listen to the howling of the wind, the tragic cries of stray dogs in the empty alley, the sound of the wonton hawker in the distance, the sound of cars returning from the dance hall by people who have leisure in the middle of the night, and the sound of the factory whistle of the nearby factory at dawn. I open my eyes and watch the night end and the day begin. After the day begins, sometimes I can sleep vaguely for a while, but at most two o'clock or so, a short time, and I wake up with a jolt, as if I have been greatly frightened. From then on, even chanting mantras can no longer put me to sleep. When I get up, every cell in my body seems to be filled with fatigue. When I lie down, I can't close my eyes. "What to do? What to do?" I used to shout like this in despair, and now I still shout like this in despair.

I don't want to see a doctor. In fact, poor people like us can't afford to see a doctor. Even if we have the strength to see a doctor once or twice, there will definitely be no result. I have long known that my disease cannot be treated with medicine. Perhaps natural recuperation will reduce the severity of the disease, but it will definitely not show results in a short period of time. Other than that, there is no better way. Long-term recuperation away from this place is not allowed by the facts, so I have to use some free time every morning and evening to take a walk in Hongkou Park with a heavy heart, trying to dissipate some of the depression in my heart, but as a result, not only can the depression not be dissipated, but I add some free air. Your and my personalities are fundamentally two typicals. You can be more tolerant than me, and I am too narrow-minded. You can not take anything seriously, and I take everything seriously. My insomnia also comes from this. In fact, in such a dark iron age, one should not be serious. I also know that my seriousness has caused me so much free air and knocked on so many nails, and in the end, I have been called a "fool" and laughed at. Thank you for your kindness, often calling me to change my quirks. However, the temper that I was born with cannot be changed, unless I am reincarnated, there may be a possibility of changing it. However, I do accept your kindness, because you are ultimately the only friend who treats me kindly. I won't talk much, so I'll stop here. I wish you well. Shiwu

Village Survey 215

— Xu Ying

I walked out of the Guandi Temple with a roll of survey forms, thinking as I walked.

Like a dream. The journey of life is full of changes. After graduating from the rural normal school, friends went east and west, like duckweed in a small pond. The duckweed gradually turned into floating clouds, moving endlessly in the north and south. For example, Yan, the person who sent me a roll of survey forms, used to be an ambitious big shot who wanted to recruit soldiers and buy horses to have great ambitions. Who would have thought that after not seeing him for two years, he had already settled into the position of statistician, and was making the slave of numbers. …

The short street was very lively. People were rushing like water, as the New Year was approaching, people were busy going to the city to do business. The main products of our village are homespun cloth, boxes woven from wicker, baskets, baskets, and small toys. The men are really as enthusiastic as gambling at this time, with sweat dripping from their heads. People who knew me kept greeting me on the road, and everyone was burying their heads on their way.

I walked and looked at the questions on those forms. Although the questions were detailed, they were easy to annoy the people who answered them. I thought, I will use this opportunity to talk to the women in the village. It's a pity, since I came here to teach, I haven't gotten a female student over the age of fifteen.

Walking to the first house in the west of the village, I knocked on the door. The "Fu" character on the door was very dim.

Someone came out, took a look through the crack in the door and said, "The boss is not at home, come back in the afternoon!" It was a woman's voice.

"I'm not necessarily looking for the boss, anyone will do," I said.

The woman went inside to coax the child, ignoring me.

After hitting several nails like this, I finally got a chance to talk to an old woman with gray hair. After asking a few questions, the old woman changed her face unexpectedly.

"What are you asking these for?" The old woman rolled her rotten eyelids "I've heard that you're hooked up with the county, asking how much land there is, do you want to increase our donations? Asking how old the old man is, do you want to kneel in the spirit basin? Asking how good the harvest is, why do you teachers ask? Isn't it like this every year? One check, one donation, more taxes. Who isn't saying that there are no good people who come from the city! …"

Covered with this unjust charge, I bit my lip and smiled bitterly again. My footsteps stepped into the next house, and my hand was gently knocking on the door knocker. I suddenly heard a vicious dog barking madly inside, and then a child, calling his mother, came out of the house to open the door. Seeing that it was me, he paused for a moment, and then immediately bowed and shouted "Teacher," so I stroked the top of his green head and asked, "Is Mom at home?"

"Sister is at home!" my little student said.

A very generous small-footed woman walked out of the second door, wearing a blue cloth pants and jacket, with a flat head and a straight face, big eyes, black hair, and a white hair rope on her head. She nodded to me slightly, and asked without shyness, "Does the teacher have anything to do with my mother?"

"It's nothing," I didn't dare to say to this enlightened rural woman, and I was surprised at the beginning. "I have a little survey, I want to ask for advice, it's about various situations in the countryside." I was afraid that she wouldn't understand this kind of talk, so I explained more, like how much land is planted? How many workers are hired? How much rent is collected every year! …

"I know," the woman took over, "When I was staying with Teacher Xiao, she also liked to ask these things, but unfortunately our country people don't know clearly, and they always think it's a donation or a tax, so they misunderstand the teachers' good intentions, and Teacher Xiao and I…"

An old shadow came to mind. I thought: Could this be Wu Er's widow? Going around in a circle, I asked my little student, "Is this your second sister?" He said yes.

She told me many things, things I wanted to know, not just about her own, she also knew clearly about the neighbors. Just as she was talking, an old woman came back from outside, and shouted as she entered the door:

"Knowing or not knowing you are staying in your mother's house, chattering nonsense with someone…"

I surveyed a few more families, and the results were not very good. The next day, Wu's child told me when he went to school: "Sister said, if you haven't finished asking, you can go this afternoon, that's when Mom goes out to play cards."

To be honest, this enlightened woman helped me for the first time in the village survey.

Winter Night 216

— Chen Fuxi

Standing in the night of December. Everything around is so quiet, so dark. - The clouds in the sky, in blocks, are jet-black and fantastic, as if they have frozen. The street lamps on the utility poles are surrounded by heavy night air. The wind is blowing the lamps, and the light on the ground is swaying there like it has been crushed. In the darkness, the houses on this small street are all closed, without any sound.

The dog is howling in the dark night.

On the street at night; calm, melancholy. The time is midnight. Standing at the entrance of Yanyi Lane, Baoshan Street, is only a young patrolman. He is wearing a black cotton coat, and from afar, he is standing straight like a night ghost. He is on duty for the safety of the residents. No matter which night, he has to stand here for three hours; within three hours, if there are thefts, assassinations, searches, fires, etc. on Baoshan Street, the heavy responsibility will be on the patrolman. For the sake of his duty, he cannot leave his post without authorization: he should be watching the movements of Baoshan every minute.

It's already past one o'clock - tonight.

He was just on duty. His shift time is at four o'clock.

Half an hour ago, he was still dozing in bed, dreaming a hazy dream: he dreamed of hiding with Qiuhua girl by the black gate and joking. He looked at her hair, eyes, breasts, hands, feet, nose, there was nothing that was not beautiful. He grabbed her hand, and as soon as he grasped it, he saw Qiuhua's face turn red, as red as peach blossoms in March; the fiery red cheeks, like those after being drunk, made him excited and crazy. Just as he was about to hug her, the dream suddenly woke up, and it was time to stand guard, so he got up, and then ran to this dark street to stand guard.

He thought, thinking of Qiuhua:

"Qiuhua this little goblin..."

Thinking this way, he couldn't help but smile. That Qiuhua, is a little goblin who lives in the third walled door of Yanyi Lane. He sees her every day when he is on duty during the day; seeing her coming out of Yanyi Lane and going into Yanyi Lane, unknowingly, they hooked up with each other.

Tonight is their date.

He had this dream and ran to Baoshan Street to stand guard. His heart always felt so uneasy; the boundless silence gave him an irresistible threat. On the soles of his feet, it seemed as if oil had been applied, and he could no longer stand steady.

"Oh. At this moment, oh. Qiuhua must be waiting for me there..."

Thinking repeatedly, his black shadow finally moved, and he tiptoed into Yanyi Lane. But in less than a quarter of an hour, the patrolman walked out of Yanyi Lane and stood in the same old place as before.

"Haha! Qiuhua this little goblin..."

Think. A slight smile appeared on his face again.

Evening (1) 217

— Qu Yi

Evening.

The sky slowly darkened. Like a snake lying in the mud, Sanxin Street also slowly stiffened at this moment, becoming almost a lead-colored street.

In early summer, the evening breeze was warm. People came out to the streets for a stroll, and very few were still wearing long gowns. The clatter of iron-soled slippers echoed on the uneven roads from time to time. Yellow rickshaw pullers, scattered here and there, each holding onto an empty rickshaw, listlessly leaning against the edge of the road: shadows of passersby were cast on the white-gray rickshaw seats from time to time.

Outside a tall Western-style building, two young men appeared at this moment. One tall and one short, a seemingly natural pair. The tall one wore a long cloth gown that did not fit well, thin and short, with Western-style pants dragging on the ground, only the pointed leather shoes visible, rising and falling, stomping on the ground with an air of overwhelming emotion. The short one wore a large-collared white shirt, the long hem reaching his knees. His developed chest had already popped three of the five buttons on the front of his shirt; wearing a pair of Chen Jiageng rubber shoes, he walked lightly across the street; at the same time, his shirt repeatedly puffed out, ostentatiously displaying his overly "inflated" chest to the depressed street.

After walking not far, this natural pair turned left. It was a small street leading to Xinsheng Road.

Although the street was small, it had a grand air. From one end to the other, there were no more than a hundred or so shops. Opium dens and medicinal plaster shops accounted for at least half. These opium dens and plaster shops were not only connected as neighbors but also competed in grandeur, flanking the road on either side.

The sidewalks were completely broken. Pieces of brick were patched together, one after another. Some places were even littered with the wash water and garbage poured out by the homeowners. But pedestrians still came and went in an endless stream. These people mostly had faces like shriveled eggplants. Their mouths were thin and blackened, their hair was withered and messy, their eyes were deeply sunken: coupled with backs arched like cats, and tattered gray-black clothes that exposed elbows and knees – they looked like skeletons freshly unearthed from the ground. Life was superfluous to them.

Yet each of them had a restless desire.

Some used greenish-blue eyes, searching for discarded cigarette butts on the sidewalk or the road; others twitched their noses, sniffing at a fragrance wafting along the street. Every time they passed an opium den with a red-lettered sign, they stopped, sniffing and inhaling repeatedly. At the same time, their eyes could not leave the opium den. Their throats rattled, yawns came in quick succession, and perhaps they would eventually collapse and die at the entrance of the opium den.
